The People Whom Allah Loves: The Ash'ari Tribe
Ibn Asakir narrates a hadith identifying the people referred to in Quran 5:54

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific identity of the people described in Quran 5:54 as identified by the Prophet (peace be upon him) through this hadith.

Core Idea
The Prophet pointed to the Ash'ari tribe as the people Allah loves.

This lesson presents a hadith from Ibn Asakir that specifies the identity of the people mentioned in Quran 5:54. The verse describes a group whom Allah loves and who love Him, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) identified them as the Ash'ari tribe of Yemen, as narrated by 'Iyad al-Ash'ari. Understanding this hadith helps clarify the context and application of the verse.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith with its chain
Notice the careful chain of transmission and the author's declaration of soundness. This shows the hadith's reliability.
The chain includes well-known narrators like Shu'ba.
2
Identify the Qur'anic verse
Recall the verse 'Soon Allah will bring a people whom He loves and they love Him' (Quran 5:54). This hadith provides its specific application.
3
Understand the Prophet's gesture
The Prophet pointed to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, indicating his tribe. This gesture identifies the people of the verse.
Abu Musa was a prominent companion from Yemen.
4
Reflect on the significance
This hadith specifies that the verse refers to the Ash'ari tribe, not merely a vague group of believers anywhere.
It highlights the virtue of the Ash'ari tribe.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ابو عبد الله الحافظ هذا حديث صحيح اخبرناه الشريف ابو القسم على بن ابراهيم الخطيب وابو الحسن على بن أحمد الفقيه قالا نا وابو منصور محمد بن عبد الملك المقرى قال انا ابو بكر أحمد بن على الخطيب انا ابو الحسن على بن محمد بن محمد الطرازى بنيسابور انا ابو حامد أحمد بن على بن حسنويه المقرى انا ابو جعفر الصائغ البغدادی واسمه محمد بن اسماعيل بن سالم نا شبابة بن سوار نا شعبة عن سماك عن عياض الأشعرى رضى الله عنه قال لما نزلت هذه الآية فسوف يأتى الله بقوم يحبهم ويحبونه) وأومأ النبى صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى أبي موسى الأشعرى رضى عنه فقال ( هم قوم هذا
Abu Abdullah al-Hafiz said: This is a sound hadith. It was reported to us by al-Sharif Abu al-Qasim Ali ibn Ibrahim al-Khatib and Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Ahmad al-Faqih, both said: and Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik al-Muqri said: informed us Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali al-Khatib: informed us Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Tarazi in Nishapur: informed us Abu Hamid Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Hasanawayh al-Muqri: informed us Abu Ja'far al-Sa'igh al-Baghdadi, named Muhammad ibn Ismail ibn Salim: narrated to us Shababa ibn Sawwar: narrated to us Shu'ba from Simak from 'Iyad al-Ash'ari (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: When this verse was revealed: 'Soon Allah will bring a people whom He loves and they love Him,' the Prophet (peace be upon him) pointed to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari (may Allah be pleased with him) and said: 'They are the people of this.'
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is a hadith narration with its full chain of transmission. The author, Ibn Asakir, first declares the hadith to be sound (sahih). He then provides his chain back to the Companion 'Iyad al-Ash'ari, who reports that when the verse 'Soon Allah will bring a people whom He loves and they love Him' (Quran 5:54) was revealed, the Prophet (peace be upon him) gestured toward Abu Musa al-Ash'ari and said 'They are the people of this' — meaning the people described in the verse are the tribe of Abu Musa, the Ash'aris of Yemen. The chain includes multiple reliable narrators, and the hadith is attributed to Shu'ba ibn al-Hajjaj, a famous hadith master. The author's purpose is to document the specific application of this Qur'anic verse, countering any generic interpretation.

Key Terms
أبو موسى الأشعري
فسوف يأتي الله بقوم يحبهم ويحبونه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the verse refers to all Muslims generally without specific identification.
Correction: This hadith specifies that the verse refers to the Ash'ari tribe of Yemen, as the Prophet pointed to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith, to whom did the Prophet point when the verse 'Soon Allah will bring a people whom He loves' was revealed?
A) The people of Yemen
B) The tribe of Banu Tamim
C) The people of Quraysh
D) The people of the Prophet's family

Key Takeaway
The hadith specifically identifies the Ash'ari tribe of Yemen as the people described in Quran 5:54.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet pointed to a specific tribe as those whom Allah loves. Do you rely on your lineage, family name, or religious label to feel secure in Allah's love, or do you actively seek the qualities that earn that love? What will you change today to move from passive belonging to active striving?
?
If you were from the Ash'ari tribe, would you feel proud and complacent, or would that honor drive you to be an even better servant? Now, realize that you are not from that tribe—so how will you respond to this hadith? Will it make you envious, hopeless, or determined to be among those whom Allah loves through your deeds?
?
The Prophet did not just say 'They are the Ash'ari tribe'; he pointed to a specific man, Abu Musa. Who is the 'Abu Musa' in your life—someone whose example shows you what it means to be loved by Allah? Are you learning from them? And more importantly, are you becoming that example for others?

The Prophet's Prayer Reaches His Descendants
Multiple hadith chains confirming the Prophet's prayer reaches descendants.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the authentic hadith evidence that the Prophet's prayer (dua) benefits not only the individual but extends to his children and descendants.

Core Idea
The Prophet's prayer reaches three generations and beyond.

This lesson presents multiple credible chains of transmission from the Companion Hudhayfa, confirming that the Prophet's supplication for a person encompasses his child, grandchild, and all descendants. It highlights the profound mercy and intercessory power of the Prophet’s prayer.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith passages
Carefully read the Arabic text and translation of the three similar hadiths. Notice the different chains (isnads) but identical meaning.
The repetition strengthens the authenticity.
2
Identify the key terms
Pay attention to the words 'صلاة' (prayer/supplication), 'تدرك' (reaches), and 'ذرية' (descendants). Understand their significance.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider what this means for a believer: the Prophet's blessing extends to one's offspring. How does this encourage seeking his intercession?
This is a mercy from Allah.

فقد أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم هبة الله بن محمد بن الحصين أنا أبو طالب محمد ابن محمد بن إبراهيم بن غيلان أنا محمد ابن عبد الله بن إبراهيم الشافعي حدثني أبو يحيى الزعفرانى جعفر بن محمد بن الحسن نا الهيثم بن يمان أبو بشر نا إسماعيل بن زكريا عن مسعر عن أبي بكر بن عمرو بن عتبة عن ابن الحذيفة عن حذيفة رضى الله عنه قال صلاة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم تدرك الرجل وولده وولد ولده ولعقبه وأخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم بن الحصين أيضاً أنا أبو على الحسن بن على التميمي أنا أحمد بن التطيعي نا عبد الله بن أحمد بن حنبل حدثني أبي نا وكيع نا أبو العميس عن أبي بكر بن عمرو بن عتبة عن ابن الحذيفة عن أبيه أن النبي صلى عليه وسلم كان إذا دعا لرجل أصابته وأصابت ولده وولده ولده. وأخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم أيضاً أنا أبو على بن المذهب أنا أبوبكر بن مالك نا عبد الله بن أحمد حدثني أبى نا أبو نعيم نا مسعر عن أبي بكر بن عمرو بن عتبة عن ابن حذيفة قال مسعر قد ذكره مرة عن حذيفة ان صلاة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لتدرك الرجل وولده وولد ولده أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم زاهر بن طاهر المستملى أنا أبو سعد محمد بن عبد الرحمن بن محمد الكنجروذى أنا أبو عمرو محمد بن أحمد بن حمدان الحيري أنا محمد بن أحمد بن عبد الله بن أبي عون الراذاني نا جبارة بن مغلس نا قيس بن الربيع عن عمرو بن مرة عن سعيد بن جبير عن ابن عباس رضى الله عنه قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ( إن ليرفع ذرية المؤمن إليه حتى يلحقهم به وإن كانوا دونه في العمل ليقربهم عينه ) ثم قرأ ( والذين آمنوا واتبعتهم ذريتهم بإيمان ألحقنا بهم ذريتهم) إلى آخر الآية رواه سفيان الثورى عن عمرو بن مرة فوقفه . أخبرناه الشيخ أبو عبد الله الفراوى أنا أبوبكر البيهقي أنا أبو عبدالله المحافظ أنا محمد بن على الصغاني بمكة نا اسحق بن إبراهيم بن عباد أنا عبد الرازق أنا الثورى عن عمرو بن مرة عن سعيد بن جبير عن ابن عباس في قوله ( ألحقنا بهم ذريتهم قال : إن الله عز وجل يرفع ذرية المؤمن معه في درجته في الجنة وإن كانوا دونه في العمل ثم قرأ ( والذين آمنوا واتبعتهم ذريتهم بإيمان ألحقنا بهم ذريتهم وما ألتناهم يقول ما نقصناهم قال البيهقي ورواه محمد بن بشر عن الثوري عن سماعة عن عمرو بن مرة وأخبرنا أبو عبد الله محمد بن الفضل أنا أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسين أنا أبر زكريا بن أبى اسحاق أنا أبو الحسن الطرائفي نا عثمان بن سعيد حدثنا عبد الله بن صالح عن معاوية بن صالح عن على بن أبي طلحة عن ابن عباس
Indeed, the Shaykh Abū al-Qāsim Hibat Allāh ibn Muḥammad ibn al-Ḥuṣayn informed us: Abū Ṭālib Muḥammad ibn Muḥammad ibn Ibrāhīm ibn Ghaylān informed us: Muḥammad ibn ʿAbd Allāh ibn Ibrāhīm al-Shāfiʿī informed us: Abū Yaḥyā al-Zaʿfarānī Jaʿfar ibn Muḥammad ibn al-Ḥasan narrated to me: al-Haytham ibn Yamān Abū Bishr narrated to us: Ismāʿīl ibn Zakariyyā narrated to us from Misʿar from Abī Bakr ibn ʿAmr ibn ʿUtba from Ibn al-Ḥudhayfa from Ḥudhayfa (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: The prayer of the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him) reaches a man and his child and his child's child and his descendants. And the Shaykh Abū al-Qāsim ibn al-Ḥuṣayn also informed us: Abū ʿAlī al-Ḥasan ibn ʿAlī al-Tamīmī informed us: Aḥmad ibn al-Ṭuṭayʿī informed us: ʿAbd Allāh ibn Aḥmad ibn Ḥanbal narrated to us: my father narrated to me: Wakīʿ narrated to us: Abū al-ʿAmays narrated to us from Abī Bakr ibn ʿAmr ibn ʿUtba from Ibn al-Ḥudhayfa from his father that the Prophet (peace be upon him), when he prayed for a man, it would befall him and his child and his child's child. And the Shaykh Abū al-Qāsim also informed us: Abū ʿAlī ibn al-Mudhahhab informed us: Abū Bakr ibn Mālik informed us: ʿAbd Allāh ibn Aḥmad narrated to us: my father narrated to me: Abū Nuʿaym narrated to us: Misʿar narrated to us from Abī Bakr ibn ʿAmr ibn ʿUtba from Ibn Ḥudhayfa—Misʿar said: He mentioned it once from Ḥudhayfa: Indeed, the prayer of the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him) reaches a man and his child and his child's child. The Shaykh Abū al-Qāsim Zāhir ibn Ṭāhir al-Mustamlī informed us: Abū Saʿd Muḥammad ibn ʿAbd al-Raḥmān ibn Muḥammad al-Kanjarūdhī informed us: Abū ʿAmr Muḥammad ibn Aḥmad ibn Ḥamdān al-Ḥayrī informed us: Muḥammad ibn Aḥmad ibn ʿAbd Allāh ibn Abī ʿAwn al-Rādhānī narrated to us: Jabbāra ibn Mughallis narrated to us: Qays ibn al-Rabīʿ narrated to us from ʿAmr ibn Murra from Saʿīd ibn Jubayr from Ibn ʿAbbās (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him) said: 'Indeed, the offspring of the believer are raised to him even if they are below him in deed, so that he may bring them near his eye.' Then he recited: 'And those who believed and whose offspring followed them in faith—We shall join their offspring to them' up to the end of the verse. Sufyān al-Thawrī narrated it from ʿAmr ibn Murra and stopped at his statement. The Shaykh Abū ʿAbd Allāh al-Farāwī informed us: Abū Bakr al-Bayhaqī informed us: Abū ʿAbd Allāh al-Ḥāfiẓ informed us: Muḥammad ibn ʿAlī al-Ṣaghānī in Makkah narrated to us: Isḥāq ibn Ibrāhīm ibn ʿAbbād narrated to us: ʿAbd al-Razzāq informed us: al-Thawrī informed us from ʿAmr ibn Murra from Saʿīd ibn Jubayr from Ibn ʿAbbās regarding His statement (We shall join their offspring to them). He said: Allah, Might and Majesty, raises the offspring of the believer with him in his rank in Paradise even if they are below him in deed. Then he recited: 'And those who believed and whose offspring followed them in faith—We shall join their offspring to them and not diminish their deeds'—he says 'not diminish'—al-Bayhaqī said: Muḥammad ibn Bishr narrated it from al-Thawrī from Samāʿa from ʿAmr ibn Murra. And Abū ʿAbd Allāh Muḥammad ibn al-Faḍl informed us: Abū Bakr Aḥmad ibn al-Ḥusayn informed us: Abū Zakariyyā ibn Abī Isḥāq informed us: Abū al-Ḥasan al-Ṭarāʾifī narrated to us: ʿUthmān ibn Saʿīd narrated to us: ʿAbd Allāh ibn Ṣāliḥ narrated to us from Muʿāwiya ibn Ṣāliḥ from ʿAlī ibn Abī Ṭalḥa from Ibn ʿAbbās.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a collection of multiple hadith chains (isnads) transmitted by Ibn ʿAsākir, all conveying similar meanings about the efficacy of the Prophet's prayer upon a person and his descendants, and about the raising of offspring to their parents' ranks in Paradise. The first hadith from Ḥudhayfa states that the Prophet's prayer 'reaches a man and his child and his child's child and his descendants.' This is repeated with slight variations in wording through different chains, emphasizing the comprehensiveness of the prayer's effect. The second major hadith is from Ibn ʿAbbās, where the Prophet says that the offspring of a believer are raised to him (in Paradise) even if they are inferior in deeds, so that he may be pleased (or 'so that he may bring them near his eye'). The Prophet then recites Qur'an 52:21: 'And those who believed and whose offspring followed them in faith—We shall join their offspring to them.' The author then includes a comment from Sufyān al-Thawrī that he stopped (i.e., did not attribute the statement to the Prophet, but as Ibn ʿAbbās's own interpretation). Then another chain from al-Bayhaqī quotes Ibn ʿAbbās explaining the verse: Allah raises the offspring of the believer to his same rank in Paradise even if they are below him in deeds, and then he recites the verse and adds that 'We do not diminish their deeds.' Al-Bayhaqī notes that Muḥammad ibn Bishr narrated it from al-Thawrī from Samāʿa from ʿAmr ibn Murra. Finally, another chain from Ibn ʿAbbās is given via different narrators. The overall purpose is to provide scriptural and hadith evidence for the doctrine that the Prophet's supplication benefits not only the person but his progeny, and that believing offspring are elevated to their parents' degrees in Paradise, as per the Qur'anic promise.

Key Terms
صلاة
تدرك
ذرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's prayer only benefits the individual personally.
Correction: The hadith explicitly states it reaches his child, grandchild, and descendants, showing it extends to his progeny.

Checkpoint
How many generations does the Prophet's prayer reach according to the first hadith?
A) Only the person
B) The person and his child
C) The person, his child, his grandchild, and descendants
D) Only descendants

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's prayer extends its blessings to a man's progeny, emphasizing his role as a mercy for all believers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The hadith teaches that the Prophet's prayer reaches a man and his descendants. Have you ever prayed specifically that the Prophet's blessings include your children and grandchildren? If not, what would it take for you to start doing so today?
?
When you read that the Prophet's prayer 'tudrik' a man and his progeny, do you sense the weight of that mercy? How does this affect your hope for your own family's faith and well-being?
?
The repeated chains emphasize the reliability of this report. Does your certainty in the Prophet's intercession for your descendants match your certainty in the report? What can you do to strengthen that reliance?

Unseen Matters
beginner
5 min
Offspring of Believers Raised in Paradise
Hadith and Qur'anic verse on the raising of believing offspring in Paradise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scriptural and hadith evidence that believing offspring are elevated to their parents' ranks in Paradise, even if they were lesser in deeds.

Core Idea
Believing offspring are joined to their parents in Paradise by Allah's grace.

This lesson presents a powerful hadith from Ibn Abbas and the supporting Qur'anic verse (52:21) to establish the glad tiding that the children of believers who follow them in faith will be raised to their parents' degree in Paradise, regardless of their own level of deeds. This is a profound mercy and a cause for joy.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and the verse
Read the hadith of the Prophet from Ibn Abbas, then the verse from the Qur'an (52:21). Notice how the Prophet recited the verse as proof.
2
Understand the explanation from Ibn Abbas
Read the interpretation given by Ibn Abbas: Allah raises the offspring to the same rank as the believer, not diminishing their deeds.
This shows the divine generosity.
3
Reflect on the condition
Note the condition 'who followed them in faith' – it is not an automatic elevation for all children, but for those who believed.
Faith is the key.

Commentary
This passage is a collection of multiple hadith chains (isnads) transmitted by Ibn ʿAsākir, all conveying similar meanings about the efficacy of the Prophet's prayer upon a person and his descendants, and about the raising of offspring to their parents' ranks in Paradise. The first hadith from Ḥudhayfa states that the Prophet's prayer 'reaches a man and his child and his child's child and his descendants.' This is repeated with slight variations in wording through different chains, emphasizing the comprehensiveness of the prayer's effect. The second major hadith is from Ibn ʿAbbās, where the Prophet says that the offspring of a believer are raised to him (in Paradise) even if they are inferior in deeds, so that he may be pleased (or 'so that he may bring them near his eye'). The Prophet then recites Qur'an 52:21: 'And those who believed and whose offspring followed them in faith—We shall join their offspring to them.' The author then includes a comment from Sufyān al-Thawrī that he stopped (i.e., did not attribute the statement to the Prophet, but as Ibn ʿAbbās's own interpretation). Then another chain from al-Bayhaqī quotes Ibn ʿAbbās explaining the verse: Allah raises the offspring of the believer to his same rank in Paradise even if they are below him in deeds, and then he recites the verse and adds that 'We do not diminish their deeds.' Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Children who are less righteous will be in a lower station in Paradise.
Correction: The hadith and verse confirm they are elevated to their parents' rank by Allah's grace.

Checkpoint
According to the explanation of Ibn Abbas, what does the verse 'Aalhaqna bihim dhurriyyatahum' mean?
A) They are separated
B) They are raised to the same rank
C) They are raised but with reduced deeds
D) They are not joined

Key Takeaway
Believing offspring are elevated to their parents' rank in Paradise by Allah's grace, as affirmed by authentic hadith and Qur'an.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
Are you more concerned about your own deeds or about ensuring your offspring follow in faith? How does this lesson shift your priorities when you think about the afterlife?

Unseen Matters
beginner
7 min
The Elevation of Believers' Offspring in Paradise
Ibn Asakir reports hadith and tafsir on God raising the offspring of believers to their level.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God, in His mercy, elevates the offspring of believers to their parents' rank in Paradise, even if the children have lesser deeds, based on the righteousness of the parents.

Core Idea
God raises the children of believers to their parents' rank in Paradise.

This lesson examines a series of hadith and Qur'anic interpretations that reveal a profound aspect of Allah's mercy: the elevation of believers' offspring to their level in the afterlife. The Prophet ﷺ himself explained this through the verse 'We will join their offspring to them,' and the Companions confirmed that children benefit from their parents' righteousness. Let us explore the textual foundation for this comforting doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Read the main hadith
Read the hadith from Ibn Abbas where the Prophet ﷺ says offspring are raised to join their parents.
Notice the recitation of verse 52:21.
2
Examine the tafsir of the verse
Ibn Abbas explains that God raises the offspring to the same rank.
This is a direct explanation of the verse.
3
Consider the second tafsir report
Another report shows the initial understanding of individual responsibility was complemented by this verse.
This shows how the verse qualifies previous understanding.
4
Reflect on the Mujahid report
Mujahid states that God rectifies the child and grandchild through the servant's righteousness.
This extends the benefit to further generations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم زاهر بن طاهر المستملى أنا أبو سعد محمد بن عبد الرحمن بن محمد الكنجروذى أنا أبو عمرو محمد بن أحمد بن حمدان الحيري أنا محمد بن أحمد بن عبد الله بن أبي عون الراذاني نا جبارة بن مغلس نا قيس بن الربيع عن عمرو بن مرة عن سعيد بن جبير عن ابن عباس رضى الله عنه قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ( إن ليرفع ذرية المؤمن إليه حتى يلحقهم به وإن كانوا دونه في العمل ليقربهم عينه ) ثم قرأ ( والذين آمنوا واتبعتهم ذريتهم بإيمان ألحقنا بهم ذريتهم) إلى آخر الآية رواه سفيان الثورى عن عمرو بن مرة فوقفه . الله أخبرناه الشيخ أبو عبد الله الفراوى أنا أبوبكر البيهقي أنا أبو عبدالله المحافظ أنا محمد بن على الصغاني بمكة نا اسحق بن إبراهيم بن عباد أنا عبد الرازق أنا الثورى عن عمرو بن مرة عن سعيد بن جبير عن ابن عباس في قوله ( ألحقنا بهم ذريتهم قال : إن الله عز وجل يرفع ذرية المؤمن معه في درجته في الجنة وإن كانوا دونه في العمل ثم قرأ ( والذين آمنوا واتبعتهم ذريتهم بإيمان ألحقنا بهم ذريتهم وما ألتناهم يقول ما نقصناهم قال البيهقي ورواه محمد بن بشر عن الثوري عن سماعة عن عمرو بن مرة وأخبرنا أبو عبد الله محمد بن الفضل أنا أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسين أنا أبو زكريا بن أبى اسحاق أنا أبو الحسن الطرائفي نا عثمان بن سعيد حدثنا عبد الله بن صالح عن معاوية بن صالح عن على بن أبي طلحة عن ابن عباس قال ( وان ليس للإنسان إلا ماسعى) فأنزل الله سبحانه بعد هذا ألحقنا بهم ذريتهم بإيمان ) فأدخل الله عز وجل الأبناء بصلاح الآباء الجنة. قالانا أبو القسم على بن إبراهيم وأبو الحسن على بن أحمد أحمد بن منصور وأبو منصور محمد بن عبدالملك بن خيرون قال أنا أبوبكر أحمد بن علی ابن ثابت الخطيب أنا محمد بن أحمد بن إبراهيم بن شادی یعنی آبا الحسن الهمذاني في مسجد عبد الله بن المبارك بقطيعة الربيع، نا أبو العباس الفضل ابن العباس الكندى بهمذان أنا أبو يعلى الموصلی نا عبدالرحمن بن سلام نا فضیل بن عیاض عن ليث عن مجاهد قال : إن الله ليصلح بصلاح العبد ولده وولد ولده .
The Shaykh Abu al-Qasim Zahir ibn Tahir al-Mustamli informed us: Abu Sa'd Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Muhammad al-Kanjruzi informed us: Abu 'Amr Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Hamdan al-Hayri informed us: Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn 'Abd Allah ibn Abi 'Awn al-Radhani narrated to us: Jabara ibn Mughallis narrated to us: Qays ibn al-Rabi' narrated to us, from 'Amr ibn Murra, from Sa'id ibn Jubayr, from Ibn 'Abbas, may God be pleased with him, who said: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: 'Indeed, the offspring of the believer are raised to him until they are joined to him, even if they are below him in deed, so that his eye may be comforted.' Then he recited: 'And those who believe and whose offspring follow them in faith — We will join their offspring to them' (52:21) to the end of the verse. Sufyan al-Thawri narrated it from 'Amr ibn Murra and stopped (at the Companion). God. We were informed by the Shaykh Abu 'Abd Allah al-Farawi: Abu Bakr al-Bayhaqi informed us: Abu 'Abd Allah al-Hafiz informed us: Muhammad ibn 'Ali al-Saghani informed us in Mecca: Ishaq ibn Ibrahim ibn 'Abbad narrated to us: 'Abd al-Razzaq informed us: al-Thawri informed us, from 'Amr ibn Murra, from Sa'id ibn Jubayr, from Ibn 'Abbas, concerning His statement 'We will join their offspring to them' — he said: 'Indeed, God, Might and Majesty, raises the offspring of the believer with him to his rank in Paradise, even if they are below him in deed.' Then he recited 'And those who believe and whose offspring follow them in faith — We will join their offspring to them and We will not deprive them of anything' — he said: 'We do not diminish them.' Al-Bayhaqi said: And Muhammad ibn Bishr narrated it from al-Thawri, from Sima', from 'Amr ibn Murra. And Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn al-Fadl informed us: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn informed us: Abu Zakariyya ibn Abi Ishaq informed us: Abu al-Hasan al-Tara'ifi informed us: 'Uthman ibn Sa'id narrated to us: 'Abd Allah ibn Salih narrated to us, from Mu'awiya ibn Salih, from 'Ali ibn Abi Talha, from Ibn 'Abbas who said: 'And that man will have only what he has striven for' (53:39). Then God, exalted, revealed after this: 'We will join their offspring to them' (52:21), so God, Might and Majesty, caused the children to enter Paradise through the righteousness of the fathers. 'Galana' Abu al-Qasim 'Ali ibn Ibrahim and Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Ahmad Ahmad ibn Mansur and Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Malik ibn Khayrun said: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn 'Ali ibn Thabit al-Khatib informed us: Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Shadi — meaning Abu al-Hasan al-Hamdani — informed us in the mosque of 'Abd Allah ibn al-Mubarak in Qati'at al-Rabi': Abu al-'Abbas al-Fadl ibn al-'Abbas al-Kindi informed us in Hamdan: Abu Ya'la al-Mawsili informed us: 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Salam narrated to us: Fudayl ibn 'Iyad narrated to us, from Layth, from Mujahid, who said: 'Indeed, God rectifies, through the righteousness of the servant, his child and his child's child.'
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of hadith and tafsir on the theme of God joining the offspring of believers to their fathers in Paradise. It begins with a marfu' hadith from Ibn 'Abbas: the Prophet (peace be upon him) said that the offspring of a believer are raised to join him, even if their deeds are lesser, so that his eye may be comforted. The Prophet then recited verse 52:21. The next report, from Ibn 'Abbas as a tafsir of the same verse, explains that God raises the offspring to the same rank in Paradise. Al-Bayhaqi adds a note about another chain. Then a third report from Ibn 'Abbas explains that initially people thought each person has only what he strove for (53:39), but then God revealed 52:21 to show that children enter Paradise through the righteousness of their fathers. Finally, a report from Mujahid states that God rectifies the child and grandchild through the righteousness of the servant. The lesson thus presents multiple proofs that the righteous deeds of a believer benefit his descendants in the Hereafter, a key doctrine affirming familial intercession.

Key Terms
ذريتهم
ألحقنا بهم
درجة
الجنة
صلاح الآباء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Each person is saved only by their own deeds; parents cannot benefit their children in the Hereafter.
Correction: Verse 52:21 and the hadith show that God, in His mercy, elevates the offspring of believing parents to their rank, even if the children have lesser deeds.

Checkpoint
According to the tafsir of Ibn 'Abbas on verse 52:21, how does God treat the offspring of believers?
A) He leaves them in a lower rank.
B) He raises them to the same rank as their fathers in Paradise.
C) He only admits them if they have equal deeds.
D) He punishes them for their fathers' sins.

Key Takeaway
The righteousness of believing parents benefits their children in the Hereafter, as God elevates them to the same rank.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you living a life that would make you eager for your children to be joined to you in Paradise, or would you prefer they be distanced from your rank because of your own shortcomings?
?
If God can elevate your children through your righteousness, what does that mean for your current level of striving in deen? Are you content with a low rank that your children might be judged by?
?
The hadith says 'so that his eye may be comforted.' Are you living in such a way that you truly desire the comfort of your children's hereafters more than their worldly success? What changes do you need to make today?

The Beauty of Abu Musa's Recitation
Ibn Asakir narrates a hadith comparing Abu Musa's voice to musical instruments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of the hadith comparing Abu Musa's voice to musical instruments and the proper understanding of such comparisons in Islamic tradition.

Core Idea
A beautiful voice in Quran recitation is likened to musical instruments, but not as endorsement.

In this passage, Ibn Asakir narrates a famous hadith about the beauty of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari's voice. The Companion Abu 'Uthman al-Nahdi compares his voice to musical instruments to convey its excellence. This lesson unpacks the narration and clarifies common misconceptions.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic text once through, then read the literal translation. Notice the chain of narration and the key comparison.
The chain is lengthy – it shows the care in transmission.
2
Identify the chain of narration
Trace the narrators from Abu 'Uthman back to the Prophet (though the hadith is mawquf). Note the names and their reliability.
This hadith is considered authentic in terms of chain.
3
Understand the comparison to musical instruments
Abu 'Uthman says he never heard a mizmar, tunbur, or sanj more beautiful than Abu Musa's voice. This is a metaphor for extreme beauty, not a judgment on instruments.
Musical instruments are not being praised; the voice is.
4
Reflect on the virtue of Abu Musa's recitation
The narrator adds that they wished he would recite Surat al-Baqarah due to his beautiful voice. This shows the impact of beautiful Quran recitation.
5
Address the misconception about musical instruments
Some mistakenly think this hadith permits music. Clarify that it merely uses instruments as a benchmark for beauty, not as a ruling on their permissibility.
This is a common misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم هبة الله بن محمد بن عبدالواحد الشيباني أنا أبو طالب محمد بن محمد بن إبراهيم بن غيلان الهمذاني، أنا أبوبكر محمد بن عبد الله بن إبراهيم الشافعي نا عبد الله ابن أحمد بن حنبل نا أبي نا معتمر عن أبيه عن أبي عثمان قال ما سمعت مزماراً ولا طنبوراً ولا صنجاً أحسن من صوت أبي موسى الأشعرى رضى الله عنه كان ليصلى بنا فنود أنه قرأ البقرة من حسن صوته.
The shaykh Abu al-Qasim Hibat Allah ibn Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Wahid al-Shaybani informed us, Abu Talib Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Ibrahim ibn Ghaylan al-Hamadhani reported to us, Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn 'Abd Allah ibn Ibrahim al-Shafi'i reported to us, 'Abd Allah ibn Ahmad ibn Hanbal reported to us, my father reported to us, Mu'tamir reported to us, from his father, from Abu 'Uthman, who said: I have not heard a mizmar (pipe), nor a tunbur (lute), nor a sanj (cymbal) more beautiful than the voice of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari (may Allah be pleased with him). He used to lead us in prayer, and we would [wish] that he recited Surat al-Baqarah due to the beauty of his voice.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is a hadith narration comparing the beauty of Abu Musa's voice to musical instruments. The chain goes through Abu 'Uthman al-Nahdi, who reports that he never heard a mizmar (a reed pipe), tunbur (a long-necked lute), or sanj (cymbals) more beautiful than Abu Musa's voice. The narrator adds that Abu Musa led them in prayer, and they wished he would recite Surat al-Baqarah (the longest chapter in the Quran) because of the beauty of his recitation. This hadith highlights the virtue of Abu Musa's recitation and the permissibility of appreciating a beautiful voice in Quran recitation, but it does not imply that musical instruments are permissible in Islam; rather, it is a comparison to express the extreme beauty of his voice.

Key Terms
أبو موسى الأشعري
مزمار
طنبور
صنج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This hadith proves that musical instruments are permissible in Islam because the Prophet (or a Companion) compared a good voice to them.
Correction: The hadith does not make a ruling on musical instruments; it simply uses them as a familiar reference point to describe the extreme beauty of Abu Musa's voice. Islamic legal rulings on music are derived from other sources.

Checkpoint
What did Abu 'Uthman say about Abu Musa's voice?
A) It was louder than a mizmar
B) He had not heard any musical instrument more beautiful than Abu Musa's voice
C) Abu Musa's voice was like a tunbur
D) He preferred the sound of a sanj over Abu Musa's voice

Key Takeaway
The hadith uses musical instruments as a metaphor to highlight the exceptional beauty of Abu Musa's Quran recitation, without ruling on the permissibility of music.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite or listen to the Quran, do you feel a longing to hear more, like the companions felt with Abu Musa? What prevents your heart from being as moved?
?
If someone compared your voice in recitation to a musical instrument, would it inspire you or offend you? Why does your reaction reveal about your intention?
?
Would you trade your daily music playlist for a beautiful recitation of Surah al-Baqarah? If not, what does that say about your love for the Quran?

Allah's Protection Against Innovations
Ibn Asakir narrates a hadith about divine appointment of protectors against innovations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the prophetic hadith about God appointing protectors against innovations and the believers' duty to defend Islam.

Core Idea
For every innovation, God raises a defender.

This hadith from Ibn 'Asakir's work reminds us that God does not abandon the Muslim community when faced with innovations. Instead, He appoints defenders who speak out and protect the faith. The lesson encourages us to recognize and support such defenders.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Read the Arabic text and translation. Note the chain of narration and the core message: God appoints a protector for each innovation.
The hadith has two chains of transmission; both are identical.
2
Understand the divine promise
The hadith says 'for every innovation by which Islam is conspired against, God appoints a protector.' Reflect on the certainty of this promise.
3
Grasp the call to action
The Prophet commands to 'seize those gatherings to defend the weak and rely on God.' This instructs believers to actively support the defenders.
The weak here may refer to those vulnerable to innovation.
4
Extract the lesson for today
Consider how this hadith applies to contemporary innovations. Recognize the ongoing role of scholars and defenders of orthodoxy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخبرنا أبو نعيم احمد بن عبدالله الحافظ نا احمد بن اسحق وعبدالله وعبد الرحمن ابنا محمد بن جعفر قالوا انا محمد بن العباس نا زكريا بن الصلت نا أبو الصلت الهروى وأخبرنا أبو البركات عبدالوهاب بن المبارك ابن احمد الأنماطى ببغداد انا أبو بكر محمد بن المظفر بن بكران الشامي انا أبو الحسن احمد بن محمد العتيق انا يوسف بن احمد بن يوسف ابن الدخيل نا أبو جعفر محمد بن عمرو العقیلی نا محمد بن أيوب بن الضريس نا عبدالسلام بن صالح وهو أبو الصلت نا عباد بن العوام نا عبد الغفار المدنى عن سعيد بن المسيب عن أبي هريرة رضى الله عنه قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ( إن الله عند كل بدعة كيد بها الإسلام وليا يذب عنه ويتكلم بعلاماته فاغتنموا تلك المجالس بالذب عن الضعفاء وتوكلوا على الله وكفى بالله وكيلا) لفظهما سواء.
Abu Nu'aym Ahmad ibn 'Abd Allah al-Hafiz informed us: Ahmad ibn Ishaq and 'Abd Allah and 'Abd al-Rahman, the two sons of Muhammad ibn Ja'far, said: Muhammad ibn al-'Abbas informed us: Zakariyya ibn al-Salt informed us: Abu al-Salt al-Harawi informed us. And Abu al-Barakat 'Abd al-Wahhab ibn al-Mubarak ibn Ahmad al-Anmati in Baghdad informed us: Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Muzaffar ibn Bakran al-Shami informed us: Abu al-Hasan Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-'Atiq informed us: Yusuf ibn Ahmad ibn Yusuf ibn al-Dakhil informed us: Abu Ja'far Muhammad ibn 'Amr al-'Uqayli informed us: Muhammad ibn Ayyub ibn al-Durays informed us: 'Abd al-Salam ibn Salih, who is Abu al-Salt, informed us: 'Abbad ibn al-'Awwam informed us: 'Abd al-Ghaffar al-Madani informed us, from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab, from Abu Hurayra, may God be pleased with him, who said: The Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, said: 'Indeed, for every innovation by which Islam is conspired against, God appoints a protector who defends it and speaks of its signs. So seize those gatherings to defend the weak, and rely on God; sufficient is God as a Trustee.' Both narrations are the same.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage presents a hadith of the Prophet (s) regarding divine support for Islam against innovations. The author, Ibn 'Asakir, provides a full chain of transmission from Abu Hurayra. The hadith states that whenever an innovation (bid'a) is plotted against Islam, God raises a protector (wali) who defends Islam and speaks about the signs of that innovation. It then exhorts believers to attend such gatherings to defend the weak and to put their trust in God. This hadith emphasizes the importance of defending orthodox doctrine against innovation and the divine promise of support for those who do so. The phrase 'لفظهما سواء' at the end indicates that the two transmission chains have identical wording.

Key Terms
بدعة
ولي
ذب
علامات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith means that every innovation is protected by God and should be accepted.
Correction: The hadith says God appoints a protector for Islam against the innovation, not that the innovation itself is protected. The protector defends Islam and exposes the innovation's signs.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith narrated by Abu Hurayra, what does God do for every innovation plotted against Islam?
A) He punishes the innovator immediately.
B) He appoints a protector who defends Islam and speaks of its signs.
C) He abandons the Muslims to face it alone.
D) He allows the innovation to spread as a test.

Key Takeaway
God guarantees that for every innovation against Islam, He will raise a defender to protect the faith and expose falsehood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever ignored a clear innovation in your mosque or community to avoid confrontation? Will you now seek to defend the truth, even if it costs you comfort?
?
The hadith commands us to 'seize those gatherings to defend the weak.' When was the last time you stood up for someone who was led astray by false teachings? What specific step will you take this week?
?
You say you rely on God, but do you actually act as if He will raise protectors, or do you hold back because you doubt His promise? How can your tawakkul become more active in the face of falsehood?

Refuting the Mu'tazila and Qadariyya Denials of Three Core Sunni Beliefs
The author identifies the Mu'tazila and Qadariyya and refutes their rejection of three core Sunni beliefs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Ibn Asakir refutes the Mu'tazila and Qadariyya rejection of the vision of Allah, the Prophet's intercession, and the punishment of the grave by citing the consensus of the Companions and the transmission of mutawatir hadiths.

Core Idea
Three beliefs denied by heretical sects are proven by consensus and mutawatir narration.

Imam Ibn Asakir begins his refutation by identifying the Mu'tazila and Qadariyya as groups whose desires led them to blind imitation and erroneous interpretation. He then specifies the three core Sunni beliefs they rejected, despite the overwhelming evidence from the Companions and the consensus of the early community. This passage establishes the Sunni position on these matters and demonstrates the method of refuting sectarian claims through transmitted authority.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how the author builds his argument: he first identifies the sects, then lists their errors, then provides the refutation.
Pay attention to the rhetorical flow from accusation to proof.
2
Identify the three denied beliefs
Find the three specific beliefs that the Mu'tazila and Qadariyya denied. List them: ru'ya, shafa'a, adhab al-qabr.
These are all matters of the unseen (sam'iyyat).
3
Understand the refutation method
The author refutes them by pointing to the consensus of the Companions and Successors, and the mutawatir nature of the hadiths. Consider why consensus is a strong argument in Sunni theology.
4
Reflect on the principle of following the Salaf
The author criticizes the sects for interpreting the Quran without authority and for abandoning the transmitted reports. This highlights the Sunni principle of relying on revelation and the early community.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما بعد فإن كثيرا من المعتزلة وأهل القدر مالت بهم أهواؤهم إلى التقليد لرؤسائهم ومن مضى من أسلافهم فتأولوا القرآن على آرائهم تأويلا لم ينزل الله به سلطانا ولا أوضح به برهانا، ولا نقلوه عن رسول رب العالمين ولا عن السلف المتقدمين فخالفوا رواية الصحابة عن نبي الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في رؤية الله بالأبصار، وقد جاءت فى ذلك الروايات من الجهات المختلفات وتواترت بها الآثار وتتابعت بها الأخبار وانكروا شفاعة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وردوا الرواية في عن السلف المتقدمين وجحدوا عذاب القبر وأن الكفار في قبورهم يعذبون وقد أجمع على ذلك الصحابة والتابعون
To proceed: Many of the Mu'tazila and the people of Qadar – their desires led them to blind imitation of their leaders and those who passed from their forefathers. So they interpreted the Quran according to their own opinions, an interpretation for which Allah sent down no authority and for which He provided no clear proof, and they did not transmit it from the Messenger of the Lord of the Worlds nor from the early predecessors (al-salaf al-mutaqaddimin). Thus they contradicted the narration of the Companions from the Prophet of Allah (ﷺ) concerning the vision of Allah with the eyes [al-ru'ya], while narrations have come about that from various directions and reports have been transmitted successively (mutawatir) and traditions have followed one after another. And they denied the intercession (al-shafa'a) of the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) and rejected the narration from the early predecessors, and they denied the punishment of the grave (adhab al-qabr) and that the disbelievers are punished in their graves, while the Companions and the Successors (al-tabi'un) have unanimously agreed upon that.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage identifies the Mu'tazila and Qadariyya as groups whose desires led them to blind imitation of their leaders, causing them to interpret the Quran according to their own opinions without divine authority or transmission from the Prophet or the Salaf. The author specifies three beliefs they rejected despite clear evidence: (1) The vision of Allah by the believers in the Hereafter – they contradicted the Companions' narration, even though the hadiths on this topic are mutawatir. (2) The intercession of the Prophet (ﷺ) – they rejected this. (3) The punishment of the grave – they denied that disbelievers are punished in their graves. The author then refutes them by citing the consensus of the Companions and Successors on these matters.

Key Terms
رؤية الله
شفاعة
عذاب القبر
المعتزلة
القدرية
الإجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila and Qadariyya claimed their interpretations were based on reason, but the author says they were blindly imitating their leaders.
Correction: The author demonstrates that these sects did not follow reason but blind imitation of their predecessors, as they rejected transmitted proofs.

Checkpoint
What three beliefs did the Mu'tazila and Qadariyya deny according to this passage?
A) Qadar, creation of Quran, and Imamate.
B) Ru'ya, shafa'a, and adhab al-qabr.
C) Tawhid, prophethood, and Resurrection.
D) Angels, scriptures, and messengers.

Key Takeaway
The Sunni position on ru'ya, shafa'a, and adhab al-qabr is established by mutawatir hadiths and the consensus of the early community, refuting the denials of the Mu'tazila and Qadariyya.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a belief that seems difficult to accept, do you find yourself leaning towards your own reasoning or the transmitted evidence from the Salaf? What does your inclination reveal about the state of your heart?
?
The Mu'tazila thought they were interpreting the Quran correctly, but the author says they were following their desires. How can you be sure that your understanding of Islam is not similarly influenced by your own desires or the opinions of modern 'leaders'?
?
The author emphasizes that these beliefs are established by mutawatir narrations and consensus. Do you treat these sources as firm and unchangeable, or do you allow doubts from contemporary intellectual trends to shake your certainty? What practical step can you take today to strengthen your conviction in the transmitted teachings?

The Quran is Uncreated Speech of Allah
Ibn Asakir affirms the Quran as uncreated and declares the created-Quran view as disbelief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position that the Quran is the uncreated speech of Allah and the ruling on those who claim it is created.

Core Idea
The Quran is Allah's eternal speech, not a created thing.

Ibn Asakir begins by affirming a foundational Sunni doctrine: the Quran is the uncreated speech of Allah. This sets a clear boundary against those who claim otherwise. Let's read his words.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic text once. Notice the clear 'wa naqool' formula. Then read the translation.
This is a direct creedal statement.
2
Identify the ruling
The passage states a ruling: whoever says the Quran is created is a disbeliever. Reflect on the seriousness of this.
This shows the importance of this doctrine.
3
Reflect on implications
Consider why the uncreatedness of the Quran is so central to Sunni theology. It relates to Allah's attributes.
The Quran is His speech, an attribute, thus eternal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونقول أن القرآن كلام الله غير مخلوق وأن من قال بخلق القرآن كان كافرا وندين أن الله يرى بالأبصار يوم القيامة كما يرى القمر ليلة البدر يراه المؤمنون كما جاءت الروايات عن الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم ونقول أن الكافرين إذا رآهم المؤمنون عن محجوبون كما قال الله عز وجل (كلا إنهم عن ربهم يومئذ لمحجوبون) سأل موسى عليه السلام ربه الرؤية في الدنيا وأن الله تجلى للجبل فجعله دكا وخر موسى صعقا فعلم موسى أنه لا يراه في الدنيا ونرى أن لا نكفر أحدا من أهل القبلة بذنب يرتكبه كالزنا والسرقة وشرب الخمر كما دانت بذلك الخوارج.
And we say that the Quran is the speech of Allah, uncreated, and that whoever says the Quran is created is a disbeliever. And we hold as religion that Allah will be seen with the eyes on the Day of Resurrection, as the moon is seen on the night of the full moon; the believers will see Him, as the narrations from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, have come. And we say that the disbelievers, when the believers see Him, are veiled from Him, as Allah, Mighty and Majestic, said (Nay, indeed, they are veiled from their Lord that Day). Moses, peace be upon him, asked his Lord for vision in this world, and Allah manifested Himself to the mountain and made it crumble, and Moses fell down unconscious; thus Moses knew that he cannot see Him in this world. And we hold the opinion that we do not excommunicate anyone among the people of the qibla (direction of prayer) for a sin he commits, such as adultery, theft, and drinking wine, as the Khawarij held.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage presents three distinct creedal positions. First, the Quran is the uncreated speech of Allah, and those who claim it is created are declared disbelievers — a strong stance in defense of orthodoxy. Second, the beatific vision (ru'yat Allah) is affirmed for the Day of Judgment, citing the famous hadith comparing seeing Allah to seeing the full moon; believers will see Him while disbelievers are veiled. The story of Moses, who could not see Allah in this world, is used to show that vision is possible only in the afterlife. Third, a key principle of Ahl al-Sunna is stated: Muslims who commit major sins are not to be excommunicated, contrary to the Khawarij and Mu'tazila. This preserves the unity of the ummah despite sin, as long as one remains within the qibla.

Key Terms
القرآن غير مخلوق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Quran is a created entity like other creations.
Correction: The Quran is the uncreated speech of Allah, part of His eternal attributes.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Asakir, what is the ruling on someone who states that the Quran is created?
A) He is a misguided innovator but still a Muslim
B) He is a disbeliever (kafir)
C) He is to be flogged
D) He is a sinner but not a disbeliever

Key Takeaway
The Quran is Allah's uncreated speech, and rejecting that places one outside the faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Quran is Allah's uncreated speech, then every time you recite it, you are uttering an eternal attribute of the Creator. How will this truth change the way you prepare for and engage in your next recitation? Make a specific resolve.
?
Do you truly treat the Quran as the uncreated speech of Allah, or do you sometimes approach it as a human text subject to your own opinions and desires? What concrete action will you take today to honor its divine origin?
?
The creed declares that denying the uncreatedness of the Quran places one outside the faith. But does your daily life reflect that belief? If the Quran is Allah's eternal speech, then it demands absolute submission. Where are you holding back from submitting to its commands?

Seeing Allah on the Day of Judgment
Ibn Asakir affirms the beatific vision for believers and the veil for disbelievers, citing proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni belief that believers will see Allah with their eyes on the Day of the Resurrection, and that disbelievers will be veiled from Him.

Core Idea
Believers will see Allah as clearly as the full moon, but not in this world.

Ibn Asakir now addresses a profound topic: the beatific vision. He affirms that Allah will be seen by the believers in the afterlife, citing the famous moon analogy and the story of Moses to show that it is only for the Hereafter.

Read the passage on vision

2
Understand the two parts

This balances affirmation with proper limits.
3
Reflect on the evidence
Ibn Asakir uses the Quranic verse about the veil and the hadith of the moon. Also uses the story of Moses to prove no vision in this world.
The evidence is both transmitted and rational.

Not Excommunicating Sinful Muslims
Ibn Asakir states the Sunni position of not excommunicating sinners among Ahl al-Qibla.

The Hadith on Choosing Close Friends
Chain and text of the hadith on friendship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the importance of choosing righteous friends as taught by the Prophet (peace be upon him) through the hadith 'A man is upon the religion of his close friend.'

Core Idea
Your close friend shapes your faith—choose wisely.

This lesson presents a famous hadith transmitted by Imam al-Khatib al-Baghdadi. The Prophet (peace be upon him) warns that a person's character and religion are influenced by his closest companion. Therefore, we must be deliberate in selecting friends.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its chain
Begin by reading the full Arabic text and English translation. Notice the chain of narrators leading back to Abu Hurayra and the Prophet (peace be upon him).
The chain shows the hadith's authenticity and transmission.
2
Understand the core message
Focus on the Prophet's statement: 'A man is upon the religion of his close friend.' Reflect on what this means about the influence of companionship.
The word 'khalil' implies an intimate, trusted friend.
3
Apply the lesson to daily life
Consider how this hadith guides your own choices of friends. Ask yourself: Do my friends encourage goodness and faith?
This hadith is often cited to emphasize the importance of righteous company.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو بكر الخطيب : بندار بن الحسين الصوفى كان من أهل الفضل المتميزين بالمعرفة والعلم، ويحكى عنه حكايات كثيرة ولم نكتب له مسندا غير حديث واحد قال أخبرنيه أبو سعد أحمد بن محمد بن أحمد بن عبدالله الماليني قال انا أبو أحمد عبد الله بن عمر بن عبدالعزيز السكري قال ثنا أبو الحسين بندار بن الحسين قال ثنا إبراهيم بن عبد الصمد قال ثنا الحسين بن الحسن قال ثنا عبد الرحمن بن مهدى قال ثنا زهير بن محمد عن موسى ابن وردان عن أبي هريرة قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ( المرء على دين خليله فلينظر احدكم من يخالل).
Abu Bakr al-Khatib said: Bandar ibn al-Husayn al-Sufi was among the people of excellence distinguished in knowledge and learning. Numerous stories are related about him, but we have not written from him a musnad (collection) except a single hadith. He said: Abu Sa'd Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Abdullah al-Malini told me, saying: Abu Ahmad Abdullah ibn Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz al-Sukkari told us, saying: Abu al-Husayn Bandar ibn al-Husayn told us, saying: Ibrahim ibn Abd al-Samad told us, saying: al-Husayn ibn al-Hasan told us, saying: Abd al-Rahman ibn Mahdi told us, saying: Zuhayr ibn Muhammad told us, from Musa ibn Wardan, from Abu Hurayra, who said: The Messenger of God, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'A man is upon the religion of his close friend, so let each of you consider whom he takes as a close friend.'
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage is a hadith transmission. Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi notes that Bandar, despite his many stories, left only this one hadith in musnad form. The chain is traced back to Abu Hurayra. The hadith itself warns that a person's character and religion are influenced by his close friend (khalil). Therefore, one should choose friends carefully. This hadith is often cited to emphasize the importance of companionship in faith.

Key Terms
خليل
دين
يخالل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith means that a person's religion is completely determined by their friends.
Correction: The hadith means that friends significantly influence one's practice and beliefs, not that they determine faith entirely.

Checkpoint
What does the hadith advise regarding friends?
A) A man should have many friends
B) A man is upon the religion of his close friend, so consider whom you befriend
C) A man should only befriend scholars
D) A man's religion is independent of friends

Key Takeaway
The hadith teaches that one's faith is affected by close friends, so choose companions who strengthen your religion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Necessity of Faith in the Messenger
Ibn Asakir explains that true faith requires belief in the messenger alongside tawhid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why faith in tawhid alone is insufficient without belief in the Prophet Muhammad and acceptance of all he conveyed about the afterlife.

Core Idea
Faith in Allah requires faith in His messenger to be complete.

Before diving into the details of the afterlife, Ibn Asakir emphasizes a foundational principle: true faith (iman) requires both the testimony of tawhid and the testimony of the messenger. This lesson establishes that the perfection of faith depends on believing everything the Prophet informed about, especially matters after death.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on faith in the messenger
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, focusing on the phrases 'منع كمال الإيمان بشهادة التوحيد' and 'ما لم يقترن به شهادة الرسول'.
Notice the strong language: 'منع كمال الإيمان' — it prevents perfection of faith.
2
Understand the relationship between the two testimonies
The passage teaches that the shahada of tawhid ('La ilaha illa Allah') must be accompanied by the shahada of the messenger ('Muhammadun Rasul Allah'). Faith is not accepted without affirming the messenger's truthfulness.
3
Extend to all news of the afterlife
The passage concludes that believers must be certain of everything the Prophet informed about after death. This sets the stage for the specific eschatological beliefs that follow.
This includes the questioning, punishment, balance, bridge, and pool.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتتمة الفصل الأول من فصول قواعد العقائد الذي يتم به الاعتقاد ولم يتفق قراءته إياه على رسول الله ﷺ ومن المصلحة إثباته ليكون الاعتقاد تاما في نفسه غير ناقص لمن أراد تحصيله وحفظه بعد قوله وأنه تعالى بعث النبي الأمى القرشي محمداً ﷺ برسالته إلى كافة العرب والعجم والجن والانس فنسخ بشرعه الشرائع إلا ما قرر ، وفضله على سائر الأنبياء وجعله سيد البشر ومنع كمال الإيمان بشهادة التوحيد وهو قول لا إله إلا الله ما لم يقترن به شهادة الرسول وهو قول محمد رسول الله فالزم الخلق تصديقه في جميع ما أخبر عنه من الدنيا والآخرة وأنه لا يتقبل إيمان عبد حتى يوقن بما أخبر عنه بعد الموت، وأوله سؤال منكر ونكير وهما شخصان مهیبان هائلان يقعدان العبد في قبره سويا ذا روح وجسد فيسألانه عن التوحيد والرسالة ويقولان من ربك وما دينك ومن نبيك ، وهما فتانا القبر وسؤالهما أول فتنة القبر بعد الموت ، وأن يؤمن بعذاب القبر وأنه حق وحكمة وعدل على الجسم والروح على ما يشاء ، . ويؤمن بالميزان ذى الكفتين واللسان وصفته في العظم أنه مثل طبـاق السموات والأرض توزن فيه الأعمال بقدرة الله تعالى والسنج يومئذ مثاقيل الذر والخردل تحقيقا لتمام العدل وتطرح صحائف الحسنات في صورة حسنة في كفة النور فيثقل بها الميزان على قدر درجاتها عند الله بفضل الله تعالى ، وتطرح صحائف السيآت في كفة الظلمة فيخف بها الميزان بعدل الله تعالى ، وأن يؤمن بأن الصراط حق وهو جسر ممدود على متن جهنم السيف وأدق من الشعر تزل عليه أقدام الكافرين بحكم الله تعالى من أحد فيهوى بهم إلى النار ويثبت عليه أقدام المؤمنين فيساقون إلى دار القرار وأن نؤمن بالحوض المورود حوض محمد ﷺ يشرب منه المؤمنون قبل دخول الجنة وبعد جواز الصراط من شرب منه شربة لم يظمأ بعدها أبداً عرضه مسيرة شهر ماؤه أشد بياضاً من اللبن وأحلى من العسل حوله أباريق عددها عدد نجوم السماء ، فيه ميزابان يصبان من الكوثر ، ويؤمن بيوم الحساب
And the completion of the first chapter of the chapters of Qawa'id al-Aqa'id, by which belief is perfected, and its recitation upon the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, did not happen. And it is beneficial to record it so that belief may be complete in itself, not deficient for whoever wants to acquire and preserve it, after his saying: 'And that He, exalted, sent the unlettered Qurayshi prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him, with His message to all Arabs and non-Arabs and jinn and humans.' So He abrogated by His law the previous laws except what He confirmed, and preferred him over the rest of the prophets and made him the master of humanity. And the perfection of faith is prevented by the testimony of tawhid, which is the saying 'There is no god but Allah', unless it is accompanied by the testimony of the messenger, which is the saying 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah'. So it is incumbent upon creation to believe him in everything he informed about of the world and the Hereafter. And that He does not accept the faith of a servant until he is certain of what he informed about after death. And the first of that is the questioning of Munkar and Nakir, who are two awesome, terrifying persons who make the servant sit in his grave both with soul and body, and ask him about tawhid and the message, saying: 'Who is your Lord? What is your religion? Who is your prophet?' And they are the two examiners of the grave, and their questioning is the first trial of the grave after death. And that one believe in the punishment of the grave, and that it is true, wisdom, and justice upon body and soul as He wills. And one believes in the balance, which has two pans and a tongue, and its description in size is like the layers of the heavens and the earth; deeds are weighed in it by the power of Allah Almighty, and the weights on that day are the weights of atoms and mustard seeds, a realization of perfect justice. And the sheets of good deeds are thrown in a goodly form into the pan of light, so the balance becomes heavy with them according to their degrees with Allah by the bounty of Allah Almighty. And the sheets of evil deeds are thrown into the pan of darkness, so the balance becomes light with them by the justice of Allah Almighty. And that one believe that the sirat is true: it is a bridge stretched over the middle of Hell, sharper than a sword and finer than a hair; the feet of the disbelievers slip on it by the decree of Allah Almighty from one side, so they fall into the Fire, while the feet of the believers are firm on it, so they are driven to the abode of permanence. And that we believe in the pool that is approached, the pool of Muhammad, peace be upon him, from which the believers drink before entering Paradise and after crossing the sirat; whoever drinks a drink from it will never thirst thereafter. Its width is a month's journey, its water is whiter than milk and sweeter than honey; around it are jugs as numerous as the stars of the sky; in it are two spouts flowing from al-Kawthar. And one believes in the Day of Reckoning.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage completes the first chapter of Qawa'id al-Aqa'id, covering eschatological beliefs that were not recited in the dream but are necessary for complete faith. It begins by reiterating the mission of Prophet Muhammad and his supremacy, then stresses that faith in tawhid is insufficient without faith in the messenger. The core of the passage is a detailed enumeration of afterlife events: 1) The questioning by the angels Munkar and Nakir in the grave, who ask about Lord, religion, and prophet. 2) Belief in the punishment of the grave as true wisdom and justice. 3) The balance (mizan) with two pans and a tongue, immense in size, where deeds are weighed with precision; good deeds cause the balance to tip by God's bounty, evil deeds by His justice. 4) The sirat (bridge) over Hell, sharper than a sword and finer than a hair; believers cross safely, disbelievers fall. 5) The Pool (hawd) of Muhammad, from which believers drink before entering Paradise; its description includes abundant water, whiteness, sweetness, and numerous vessels. 6) Belief in the Day of Reckoning (yawm al-hisab). All these beliefs are to be affirmed as true.

Key Terms
شهادة التوحيد
شهادة الرسول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that simply believing in Allah (tawhid) is sufficient for faith, without belief in the Prophet.
Correction: This passage explicitly states that perfection of faith is prevented if the testimony of the messenger is not combined with the testimony of tawhid. True faith requires both.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what prevents perfect faith (kamaal al-iman)?
A) Disbelief in the angels
B) Lack of charity
C) Not accompanying the testimony of tawhid with the testimony of the messenger
D) Doubting the punishment of the grave

Key Takeaway
Faith in Allah is only complete when combined with faith in His messenger and acceptance of all he conveyed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself believing in Allah yet feeling hesitant or doubtful about something the Prophet said about the afterlife? What is that thing, and what will you do today to replace doubt with certainty?
?
If your faith in Allah is not accompanied by complete submission to every command and report of His messenger, is it really faith? Search your heart: where have you been picking and choosing what to accept?
?
You claim to love Allah, but do you love His messenger enough to trust him completely? What practical step can you take this week to increase your certainty in his guidance?

The Questioning in the Grave and Its Punishment
Ibn Asakir describes the questioning by Munkar and Nakir and affirms grave punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first trial after death: the questioning by the angels Munkar and Nakir and the reality of grave punishment for both body and soul.

Core Idea
The first test after death is the questioning in the grave by two awesome angels.

Having established the necessity of believing all that the Prophet informed about the afterlife, Ibn Asakir now details the first event after death: the questioning by Munkar and Nakir. This lesson covers their identity, the questions they ask, and the belief that grave punishment is true and affects both body and soul.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of Munkar and Nakir
Read the Arabic passage describing the two angels: they are awesome, terrifying, and make the servant sit in the grave with soul and body.
Note the phrase 'سويا ذا روح وجسد' — with soul and body together.
2
Understand the questions asked
The angels ask three questions: 'Who is your Lord? What is your religion? Who is your prophet?' These are the core of the first trial.
3
Affirm belief in grave punishment
The passage then commands belief that the punishment of the grave is true, wise, and just, affecting body and soul as Allah wills.
This refutes those who claim punishment is only spiritual.

What do the angels Munkar and Nakir ask the deceased?
A) How they performed their prayers
B) About their wealth and children
C) Who is your Lord, what is your religion, who is your prophet?
D) About their intentions

The first fitna after death is the questioning by Munkar and Nakir, covering Lord, religion, and prophet, and the punishment of the grave is real and affects both body and soul.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the angels were to appear to you right now and ask 'Who is your Lord?', what evidence from your daily life would your answer be based on? Are you truly certain, or just assuming?
?
The passage says the punishment of the grave is 'justice upon body and soul'. What have you done today—in thought, word, or deed—that would either alleviate or increase that punishment?
?
Munkar and Nakir are described as 'awesome, terrifying'. How does the reality of facing them change what you fear most? Are you more concerned with people's opinions or with that inevitable encounter?

The Balance (Mizan) and Weighing of Deeds
Ibn Asakir describes the balance with two pans and its function in weighing deeds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the scale on which deeds are weighed, its description, and how God's bounty and justice affect the outcome.

Core Idea
The scale with two pans and a tongue weighs deeds with perfect justice, even atoms.

After the grave, the next major event is the weighing of deeds on a cosmic scale. Ibn Asakir provides a vivid description of the mizan, its immense size, the precision of its weights, and how the sheets of deeds are placed in pans of light and darkness, reflecting divine bounty and justice.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of the balance
Read the Arabic passage about the balance, noting its two pans (kiftayn) and tongue (lisan), and its size like the layers of heavens and earth.
'السنج' refers to the weights, which are atoms and mustard seeds.
2
Understand the weighing process
Deeds are written on sheets (sahaif). Good deeds are thrown in a goodly form into the pan of light, making it heavy by God's bounty; evil deeds are thrown in the pan of darkness, making it light by God's justice.
Notice that the heaviness of the good deeds is attributed to God's bounty (fadl), while the lightness of evil deeds is by His justice (adl).
3
Appreciate the precision
The weights are as small as atoms and mustard seeds (mithaqil al-dharra wal-khardal), emphasizing perfect justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتتمة الفصل الأول من فصول قواعد العقائد الذي يتم به الاعتقاد ولم يتفق قراءته إياه على رسول الله ﷺ ومن المصلحة إثباته ليكون الاعتقاد تاما في نفسه غير ناقص لمن أراد تحصيله وحفظه بعد قوله وأنه تعالى بعث النبي الأمى القرشي محمداً ﷺ برسالته إلى كافة العرب والعجم والجن والانس فنسخ بشرعه الشرائع إلا ما قرر ، وفضله على سائر الأنبياء وجعله سيد البشر ومنع كمال الإيمان بشهادة التوحيد وهو قول لا إله إلا الله ما لم يقترن به شهادة الرسول وهو قول محمد رسول الله فالزم الخلق تصديقه في جميع ما أخبر عنه من الدنيا والآخرة وأنه لا يتقبل إيمان عبد حتى يوقن بما أخبر عنه بعد الموت، وأوله سؤال منكر ونكير وهما شخصان مهیبان هائلان يقعدان العبد في قبره سويا ذا روح وجسد فيسألانه عن التوحيد والرسالة ويقولان من ربك وما دينك ومن نبيك ، وهما فتانا القبر وسؤالهما أول فتنة القبر بعد الموت ، وأن يؤمن بعذاب القبر وأنه حق وحكمة وعدل على الجسم والروح على ما يشاء ، . ويؤمن بالميزان ذى الكفتين واللسان وصفته في العظم أنه مثل طبـاق السموات والأرض توزن فيه الأعمال بقدرة الله تعالى والسنج يومئذ مثاقيل الذر والخردل تحقيقا لتمام العدل وتطرح صحائف الحسنات في صورة حسنة في كفة النور فيثقل بها الميزان على قدر درجاتها عند الله بفضل الله تعالى ، وتطرح صحائف السيآت في كفة الظلمة فيخف بها الميزان بعدل الله تعالى ، وأن يؤمن بأن الصراط حق وهو جسر ممدود على متن جهنم السيف وأدق من الشعر تزل عليه أقدام الكافرين بحكم الله تعالى من أحد فيهوى بهم إلى النار ويثبت عليه أقدام المؤمنين فيساقون إلى دار القرار وأن نؤمن بالحوض المورود حوض محمد ﷺ يشرب منه المؤمنون قبل دخول الجنة وبعد جواز الصراط من شرب منه شربة لم يظمأ بعدها أبداً عرضه مسيرة شهر ماؤه أشد بياضاً من اللبن وأحلى من العسل حوله أباريق عددها عدد نجوم السماء ، فيه ميزابان يصبان من الكوثر ، ويؤمن بيوم الحساب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The balance is metaphorical or only spiritual.
Correction: The passage gives a physical description with two pans and a tongue, and deeds are weighed with actual weights, indicating a real, tangible balance.

Checkpoint
What causes the balance to become heavy with good deeds?
A) The number of deeds
B) The bounty of Allah
C) The justice of Allah
D) The size of the sheets

Key Takeaway
The balance weighs deeds with perfect justice, where good deeds tip the scale by God's bounty and evil deeds by His justice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every deed—even the weight of a mustard seed—is placed on the scale, what deed have you done today that you hope will tip the balance towards mercy, and how can you increase such deeds before you stand before that scale?
?
The passage says good deeds are weighed 'by the bounty of Allah' and evil deeds 'by His justice.' Which of these two realities do you rely on more in your daily life—God’s bounty or His justice—and how does that affect the way you repent or persevere in obedience?
?
Imagine the scale towering like the heavens and the earth, with your deeds in two piles. Are you satisfied with the weight of your current state? What specific action will you take this week to add to the pan of light, knowing it will be weighed with atomic precision?

The Bridge (Sirat) Over Hell
Ibn Asakir describes the sirat bridge and the crossing of believers and disbelievers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the sirat bridge, its description, and how believers and disbelievers cross it differently.

Core Idea
The sirat is a sharper-than-sword, finer-than-hair bridge over Hell; believers cross safely, disbelievers fall.

After the weighing of deeds, the next stage is crossing the sirat, a bridge stretched over Hell. Ibn Asakir describes its terrifying sharpness and thinness, and the contrasting fates of believers and disbelievers upon it. This lesson emphasizes the reality of this bridge and its role in divine justice.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of the sirat
Read the Arabic passage: the sirat is a bridge over Hell, sharper than a sword and finer than a hair.
Notice the words 'جسر ممدود على متن جهنم'.
2
Understand the fate of disbelievers
The feet of disbelievers slip on it by Allah's decree, and they fall into the Fire.
The phrase 'تزل عليه أقدام الكافرين بحكم الله تعالى'.
3
Understand the fate of believers
The feet of believers are firm on it, and they are driven to the abode of permanence (Paradise).
Note the contrast: slipping vs. firmness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتتمة الفصل الأول من فصول قواعد العقائد الذي يتم به الاعتقاد ولم يتفق قراءته إياه على رسول الله ﷺ ومن المصلحة إثباته ليكون الاعتقاد تاما في نفسه غير ناقص لمن أراد تحصيله وحفظه بعد قوله وأنه تعالى بعث النبي الأمى القرشي محمداً ﷺ برسالته إلى كافة العرب والعجم والجن والانس فنسخ بشرعه الشرائع إلا ما قرر ، وفضله على سائر الأنبياء وجعله سيد البشر ومنع كمال الإيمان بشهادة التوحيد وهو قول لا إله إلا الله ما لم يقترن به شهادة الرسول وهو قول محمد رسول الله فالزم الخلق تصديقه في جميع ما أخبر عنه من الدنيا والآخرة وأنه لا يتقبل إيمان عبد حتى يوقن بما أخبر عنه بعد الموت، وأوله سؤال منكر ونكير وهما شخصان مهیبان هائلان يقعدان العبد في قبره سويا ذا روح وجسد فيسألانه عن التوحيد والرسالة ويقولان من ربك وما دينك ومن نبيك ، وهما فتانا القبر وسؤالهما أول فتنة القبر بعد الموت ، وأن يؤمن بعذاب القبر وأنه حق وحكمة وعدل على الجسم والروح على ما يشاء ، . ويؤمن بالميزان ذى الكفتين واللسان وصفته في العظم أنه مثل طبـاق السموات والأرض توزن فيه الأعمال بقدرة الله تعالى والسنج يومئذ مثاقيل الذر والخردل تحقيقا لتمام العدل وتطرح صحائف الحسنات في صورة حسنة في كفة النور فيثقل بها الميزان على قدر درجاتها عند الله بفضل الله تعالى ، وتطرح صحائف السيآت في كفة الظلمة فيخف بها الميزان بعدل الله تعالى ، وأن يؤمن بأن الصراط حق وهو جسر ممدود على متن جهنم السيف وأدق من الشعر تزل عليه أقدام الكافرين بحكم الله تعالى من أحد فيهوى بهم إلى النار ويثبت عليه أقدام المؤمنين فيساقون إلى دار القرار وأن نؤمن بالحوض المورود حوض محمد ﷺ يشرب منه المؤمنون قبل دخول الجنة وبعد جواز الصراط من شرب منه شربة لم يظمأ بعدها أبداً عرضه مسيرة شهر ماؤه أشد بياضاً من اللبن وأحلى من العسل حوله أباريق عددها عدد نجوم السماء ، فيه ميزابان يصبان من الكوثر ، ويؤمن بيوم الحساب
And the completion of the first chapter of the chapters of Qawa'id al-Aqa'id, by which belief is perfected, and its recitation upon the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, did not happen. And it is beneficial to record it so that belief may be complete in itself, not deficient for whoever wants to acquire and preserve it, after his saying: 'And that He, exalted, sent the unlettered Qurayshi prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him, with His message to all Arabs and non-Arabs and jinn and humans.' So He abrogated by His law the previous laws except what He confirmed, and preferred him over the rest of the prophets and made him the master of humanity. And the perfection of faith is prevented by the testimony of tawhid, which is the saying 'There is no god but Allah', unless it is accompanied by the testimony of the messenger, which is the saying 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah'. So it is incumbent upon creation to believe him in everything he informed about of the world and the Hereafter. And that He does not accept the faith of a servant until he is certain of what he informed about after death. And the first of that is the questioning of Munkar and Nakir, who are two awesome, terrifying persons who make the servant sit in his grave both with soul and body, and ask him about tawhid and the message, saying: 'Who is your Lord? What is your religion? Who is your prophet?' And they are the two examiners of the grave, and their questioning is the first trial of the grave after death. And that one believe in the punishment of the grave, and that it is true, wisdom, and justice upon body and soul as He wills. And one believes in the balance, which has two pans and a tongue, and its description in size is like the layers of the heavens and the earth; deeds are weighed in it by the power of Allah Almighty, and the weights on that day are the weights of atoms and mustard seeds, a realization of perfect justice. And the sheets of good deeds are thrown in a goodly form into the pan of light, so the balance becomes heavy with them according to their degrees with Allah by the bounty of Allah Almighty. And the sheets of evil deeds are thrown into the pan of darkness, so the balance becomes light with them by the justice of Allah Almighty. And that one believe that the sirat is true: it is a bridge stretched over the middle of Hell, sharper than a sword and finer than a hair; the feet of the disbelievers slip on it by the decree of Allah Almighty from one side, so they fall into the Fire, while the feet of the believers are firm on it, so they are driven to the abode of permanence. And that we believe in the pool that is approached, the pool of Muhammad, peace be upon him, from which the believers drink before entering Paradise and after crossing the sirat; whoever drinks a drink from it will never thirst thereafter. Its width is a month's journey, its water is whiter than milk and sweeter than honey; around it are jugs as numerous as the stars of the sky; in it are two spouts flowing from al-Kawthar. And one believes in the Day of Reckoning.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage completes the first chapter of Qawa'id al-Aqa'id, covering eschatological beliefs that were not recited in the dream but are necessary for complete faith. It begins by reiterating the mission of Prophet Muhammad and his supremacy, then stresses that faith in tawhid is insufficient without faith in the messenger. The core of the passage is a detailed enumeration of afterlife events: 1) The questioning by the angels Munkar and Nakir in the grave, who ask about Lord, religion, and prophet. 2) Belief in the punishment of the grave as true wisdom and justice. 3) The balance (mizan) with two pans and a tongue, immense in size, where deeds are weighed with precision; good deeds cause the balance to tip by God's bounty, evil deeds by His justice. 4) The sirat (bridge) over Hell, sharper than a sword and finer than a hair; believers cross safely, disbelievers fall. 5) The Pool (hawd) of Muhammad, from which believers drink before entering Paradise; its description includes abundant water, whiteness, sweetness, and numerous vessels. 6) Belief in the Day of Reckoning (yawm al-hisab). All these beliefs are to be affirmed as true.

Key Terms
الصراط
جهنم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to the feet of disbelievers on the sirat?
A) They become firm
B) They slip and they fall into the Fire
C) They walk slowly
D) They are lifted by angels

Key Takeaway
The sirat is a real bridge over Hell; believers cross firmly to Paradise, while disbelievers slip and fall into the Fire.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Sirat is sharper than a sword and finer than a hair, and your footing depends on your faith and deeds, what are you doing today to ensure your feet will be firm when you cross it?
?
The disbelievers' feet slip by Allah's decree. But you believe. Yet, do you feel the weight of that belief in your daily choices, or do you live as if the Sirat is far away?
?
The bridge is real. Your crossing is certain. What is one fear you have about your own crossing, and what one verse or hadith can you recall today to strengthen your hope in Allah's mercy?
