The Pool (Hawd) of Muhammad and the Day of Reckoning
Ibn Asakir describes the Prophet's pool and affirms belief in the Day of Reckoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the description of the Prophet's pool, from which believers drink before entering Paradise, and the belief in the Day of Reckoning.

Core Idea
The Prophet's pool quenches believers forever before Paradise, and the Day of Judgment is true.

The final eschatological beliefs in this passage are the Pool (hawd) of Muhammad and the Day of Reckoning. Ibn Asakir provides a vivid description of the pool's size, water, and abundance, emphasizing that whoever drinks from it will never thirst again. The lesson concludes with the simple yet foundational belief in the Day of Account.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of the pool
Read the Arabic passage: the pool is for believers, before entering Paradise and after crossing the sirat. Its water is whiter than milk and sweeter than honey, and its width is a month's journey.
Note the phrase 'عرضه مسيرة شهر'.
2
Understand the properties of the pool
It has jugs as numerous as stars, and two spouts flow from al-Kawthar. Drinking from it eliminates thirst forever.
Compare with descriptions in hadith.
3
Affirm belief in the Day of Reckoning
The passage ends with a command to believe in Yawm al-Hisab, the Day of Account.
This is the final item in the list of beliefs.

4 min
Belief in the Punishment of the Grave
Ibn Asakir affirms the punishment of the grave as true, wise, and just.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the punishment of the grave is a true, wise, and just decree affecting both body and soul as Allah wills.

Core Idea
The punishment of the grave is real, just, and encompasses body and soul.

Ibn Asakir begins this creedal statement by affirming the reality of the punishment of the grave. This belief is fundamental to Islamic eschatology, reminding believers that accountability begins immediately after death. The passage succinctly states its attributes: truth, wisdom, and justice.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic sentence once without translating. Let the wording 'حق وحكمة وعدل' sink in.
The three attributes are packed into a short phrase.
2
Identify the three attributes
Note that the punishment is described as true (حق), wise (حكمة), and just (عدل). Each has a distinct meaning.
Truth means it is real; wisdom means it has purpose; justice means it is fair.
3
Reflect on the scope
The phrase 'على الجسم والروح' indicates the punishment affects both body and soul. Think about why this is important.
It rejects purely spiritual interpretations.
4
Consider its placement
Why is this belief listed first among eschatological matters? The grave is the first stage of the afterlife.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويؤمن بعذاب القبر وأنه حق وحكمة وعدل على الجسم والروح على ما يشاء ، . ويؤمن بالميزان ذى الكفتين واللسان وصفته في العظم أنه مثل طبـاق السموات والأرض توزن فيه الأعمال بقدرة الله تعالى والسنج يومئذ مثاقيل الذر والخردل تحقيقا لتمام العدل وتطرح صحائف الحسنات في صورة حسنة في كفة النور فيثقل بها الميزان على قدر درجاتها عند الله بفضل الله تعالى ، وتطرح صحائف السيآت في كفة الظلمة فيخف بها الميزان بعدل الله تعالى ، وأن يؤمن بأن الصراط حق وهو جسر ممدود على متن جهنم السيف وأدق من الشعر تزل عليه أقدام الكافرين بحكم الله تعالى من أحد فيهوى بهم إلى النار ويثبت عليه أقدام المؤمنين فيساقون إلى دار القرار وأن نؤمن بالحوض المورود حوض محمد يشرب منه المؤمنون قبل دخول الجنة وبعد جواز الصراط من شرب منه شربة لم يظمأ بعدها أبداً عرضه مسيرة شهر ماؤه أشد بياضاً من اللبن وأحلى من العسل حوله أباريق عددها عدد نجوم السماء ، فيه ميزابان يصبان من الكوثر ، ويؤمن بيوم الحساب
And he believes in the punishment of the grave, and that it is true, and wise, and just, upon the body and soul as He wills. And he believes in the scale (mizan) with two pans and a tongue, and its description in greatness is that it is like the layers of the heavens and the earth; deeds are weighed in it by the power of Allah Almighty, and the weights on that day are the weights of atoms and mustard seeds, fulfillment of complete justice. And the pages of good deeds are thrown in a beautiful form into the pan of light, so the scale becomes heavy with them according to their degrees with Allah, by the grace of Allah Almighty. And the pages of evil deeds are thrown in the pan of darkness, so the scale becomes light with them by the justice of Allah Almighty. And he believes that the path (sirat) is true, and it is a bridge stretched over the middle of Hell, like a sword, and finer than a hair; the feet of the disbelievers slip on it by the decree of Allah Almighty, so they fall into the Fire, and the feet of the believers are made firm on it, so they are driven to the Abode of Permanence. And we believe in the watered cistern (hawd) – the cistern of Muhammad (peace be upon him), from which the believers drink before entering Paradise and after crossing the sirat; whoever drinks a drink from it will never thirst after it forever. Its width is a month's journey, its water is whiter than milk and sweeter than honey; around it are jugs equal in number to the stars of the sky; in it are two spouts flowing from al-Kawthar. And he believes in the Day of Reckoning.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage is a creedal enumeration of several eschatological beliefs that a Muslim must hold. It covers five topics: punishment of the grave, the scale (mizan), the bridge (sirat), the cistern (hawd) of the Prophet, and the Day of Reckoning. First, belief in the punishment of the grave is affirmed: it is true, wise, and just, affecting both body and soul as Allah wills. Second, the scale is described: it has two pans and a tongue; its size is comparable to the heavens and earth; deeds are weighed by Allah's power; the weights are atoms and mustard seeds, ensuring perfect justice. Good deeds are cast into a light-filled pan, causing it to weigh heavy by Allah's grace; evil deeds are cast into a dark pan, causing lightness by Allah's justice. Third, the sirat is a true bridge stretched over the middle of Hell, like a sword and finer than a hair. The disbelievers' feet slip and they fall into the Fire; the believers' feet are made firm and they proceed to Paradise. Fourth, the cistern of Muhammad is described: believers drink from it before entering Paradise and after crossing the sirat; its water is whiter than milk, sweeter than honey, and never causes thirst; its width is a month's journey; it has jugs like stars and two spouts from the river of Kawthar. Fifth, belief in the Day of Reckoning is required.

Key Terms
عذاب القبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the punishment of the grave is purely spiritual or metaphorical.
Correction: The passage affirms it is real and affects both body and soul.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT an attribute of the punishment of the grave mentioned in the passage?
A) True (حق)
B) Wise (حكمة)
C) Just (عدل)
D) Merciful (رحمة)

Key Takeaway
The punishment of the grave is a true, wise, and just reality that affects both body and soul as Allah wills.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every deed, even the hidden ones, will be met with justice in the grave? What would you change today if you knew the punishment were immediate and unavoidable?
?
How does the reality of the grave's punishment, affecting both body and soul, influence your daily choices? What habit are you clinging to that you would abandon if you felt the weight of this truth?
?
If the punishment of the grave is both wise and just, how are you preparing your soul and body for that moment? What specific act of worship or repentance will you commit to starting today?

Belief in the Scale (Mizan)
Ibn Asakir describes the scale and its function in weighing deeds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the description and function of the scale used to weigh deeds on the Day of Judgment.

Core Idea
The scale has two pans, is vast like the heavens and earth, and deeds are weighed with perfect justice.

Ibn Asakir provides a detailed description of the scale, emphasizing its grandeur and precision. This belief underscores that every deed will be accounted for, from the weight of an atom to the pages of good and evil actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage on the mizan
Read the full passage describing the scale. Notice the physical details and the process.
The passage is relatively long; take your time.
2
Note the physical description
The scale has two pans (كفتين) and a tongue (لسان). Its size is like the layers of the heavens and earth.
This emphasizes its vastness.
3
Understand the weighing process
Good deeds in the form of pages are thrown into the pan of light, making it heavy by grace. Evil deeds into the pan of darkness, making it light by justice.
The contrast between grace and justice is key.
4
Reflect on the atomic weights
The weights are atoms and mustard seeds, showing Allah's complete justice in accounting for even the smallest deeds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويؤمن بعذاب القبر وأنه حق وحكمة وعدل على الجسم والروح على ما يشاء ، . ويؤمن بالميزان ذى الكفتين واللسان وصفته في العظم أنه مثل طبـاق السموات والأرض توزن فيه الأعمال بقدرة الله تعالى والسنج يومئذ مثاقيل الذر والخردل تحقيقا لتمام العدل وتطرح صحائف الحسنات في صورة حسنة في كفة النور فيثقل بها الميزان على قدر درجاتها عند الله بفضل الله تعالى ، وتطرح صحائف السيآت في كفة الظلمة فيخف بها الميزان بعدل الله تعالى ، وأن يؤمن بأن الصراط حق وهو جسر ممدود على متن جهنم السيف وأدق من الشعر تزل عليه أقدام الكافرين بحكم الله تعالى من أحد فيهوى بهم إلى النار ويثبت عليه أقدام المؤمنين فيساقون إلى دار القرار وأن نؤمن بالحوض المورود حوض محمد يشرب منه المؤمنون قبل دخول الجنة وبعد جواز الصراط من شرب منه شربة لم يظمأ بعدها أبداً عرضه مسيرة شهر ماؤه أشد بياضاً من اللبن وأحلى من العسل حوله أباريق عددها عدد نجوم السماء ، فيه ميزابان يصبان من الكوثر ، ويؤمن بيوم الحساب
And he believes in the punishment of the grave, and that it is true, and wise, and just, upon the body and soul as He wills. And he believes in the scale (mizan) with two pans and a tongue, and its description in greatness is that it is like the layers of the heavens and the earth; deeds are weighed in it by the power of Allah Almighty, and the weights on that day are the weights of atoms and mustard seeds, fulfillment of complete justice. And the pages of good deeds are thrown in a beautiful form into the pan of light, so the scale becomes heavy with them according to their degrees with Allah, by the grace of Allah Almighty. And the pages of evil deeds are thrown in the pan of darkness, so the scale becomes light with them by the justice of Allah Almighty. And he believes that the path (sirat) is true, and it is a bridge stretched over the middle of Hell, like a sword, and finer than a hair; the feet of the disbelievers slip on it by the decree of Allah Almighty, so they fall into the Fire, and the feet of the believers are made firm on it, so they are driven to the Abode of Permanence. And we believe in the watered cistern (hawd) – the cistern of Muhammad (peace be upon him), from which the believers drink before entering Paradise and after crossing the sirat; whoever drinks a drink from it will never thirst after it forever. Its width is a month's journey, its water is whiter than milk and sweeter than honey; around it are jugs equal in number to the stars of the sky; in it are two spouts flowing from al-Kawthar. And he believes in the Day of Reckoning.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage is a creedal enumeration of several eschatological beliefs that a Muslim must hold. It covers five topics: punishment of the grave, the scale (mizan), the bridge (sirat), the cistern (hawd) of the Prophet, and the Day of Reckoning. First, belief in the punishment of the grave is affirmed: it is true, wise, and just, affecting both body and soul as Allah wills. Second, the scale is described: it has two pans and a tongue; its size is comparable to the heavens and earth; deeds are weighed by Allah's power; the weights are atoms and mustard seeds, ensuring perfect justice. Good deeds are cast into a light-filled pan, causing it to weigh heavy by Allah's grace; evil deeds are cast into a dark pan, causing lightness by Allah's justice. Third, the sirat is a true bridge stretched over the middle of Hell, like a sword and finer than a hair. The disbelievers' feet slip and they fall into the Fire; the believers' feet are made firm and they proceed to Paradise. Fourth, the cistern of Muhammad is described: believers drink from it before entering Paradise and after crossing the sirat; its water is whiter than milk, sweeter than honey, and never causes thirst; its width is a month's journey; it has jugs like stars and two spouts from the river of Kawthar. Fifth, belief in the Day of Reckoning is required.

Belief in the Bridge (Sirat)
Ibn Asakir describes the sirat and its function.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the sirat as a bridge over Hell and the fate of believers and disbelievers upon it.

Core Idea
The sirat is a sharp, thin bridge over Hell; believers cross safely, disbelievers fall.

Ibn Asakir describes the sirat as a real bridge that spans Hell, sharper than a sword and finer than a hair. This belief emphasizes the role of divine decree in salvation and perdition.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage on the sirat
Read the sentence describing the bridge. Focus on its physical characteristics.
2
Note the physical description
The sirat is a bridge over the middle of Hell, like a sword, and finer than a hair. This shows its sharpness and thinness.
It is a real, tangible object.
3
Understand the outcomes
Disbelievers slip and fall into the Fire by Allah's decree. Believers are made firm and proceed to Paradise.
This is a matter of divine will.
4
Reflect on 'Dar al-Qarar'
Paradise is called the Abode of Permanence, emphasizing eternity.

The Reckoning and Its Variations
Ibn Asakir describes the varying degrees of reckoning and the questions asked to different groups.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different types of reckoning on the Day of Judgment and that Allah questions prophets, disbelievers, innovators, and Muslims about different matters.

Core Idea
Reckoning varies by rank: some face scrutiny, some leniency, and some enter Paradise without account.

This passage from Ibn Asakir's creed explains that not everyone will be held to the same standard on the Day of Judgment. People differ in how they are reckoned, and even the questions they are asked depend on who they are. This lesson explores the details of this reckoning as part of Sunni belief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about reckoning
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note the three categories of reckoning mentioned.
2
Identify the three categories
Find the three types: those scrutinized, those shown leniency, and those entering Paradise without reckoning (muqarrabun).
3
Notice the different groups questioned
The passage lists prophets, disbelievers, innovators, and Muslims. Reflect on why each group is asked specific questions.
Prophets about the message, disbelievers about denial, innovators about Sunnah, Muslims about deeds.
4
Ask why this matters
Consider how this teaching shows Allah's justice and mercy. Not everyone is judged the same way.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتفاوت الخلق فيه إلى مناقش فى الحساب وإلى مسامح فيه ، إلى من يدخل الجنة بغير حساب وهم المقربون فيسأل من شاء من الأنبياء عن تبليغ الرسالة ومن شاء من الكفار عن تكذيب المرسلين ويسأل المبتدعة عن السنة ويسأل المسلمين عن الأعمال ويؤمن بإخراج الموحدين من النار بعد الانتقام حتى لا يبقى في جهنم موحد بفضل الله تعالى ، ويؤمن بشفاعة الأنبياء ثم العلماء ثم الشهداء ثم سائر المؤمنين كل على حسب جاهه ومنزلته ، ومن بقى من المؤمنين ولم يكن له شفيع أخرج بفضل الله تعالى ولا يخلد في النار مؤمن بل يخرج منها من كان في قلبه مثقال ذرة من الإيمان ، وأن يعتقد فضل الصحابة وترتيبهم وأن أفضل الناس بعد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أبو بكر ثم عمر ثم عثمان ثم على رضى الله عنهم ، وأن يحسن الظن بجميع الصحابة ويثني عليهم كما أثنى الله تعالى ورسوله عليه السلام وعليهم أجمعين فكل ذلك لما وردت به الاخبار وشهدت به الآثار فمن اعتقد جميع ذلك موقنا به كان من أهل الحق وعصابة السنة وفارق رهط الضلال والبدعة فنسأل الله تعالى كمال اليقين والثبات في الدين لنا ولكافة المسلمين إنه أرحم الراحمين وصلى الله على محمد وآله أجمعين
And the disparity of creation in it: some are scrutinized in the reckoning, some are granted leniency, some enter Paradise without reckoning – and they are the close ones (muqarrabun). And He asks whomever He wills of the prophets about delivering the message, and whomever He wills of the disbelievers about denying the messengers, and He asks the innovators (mubtadi'ah) about the Sunnah, and He asks the Muslims about deeds. And he believes in the removal of the monotheists from the Fire after punishment until no monotheist remains in Hell, by the grace of Allah Almighty. And he believes in the intercession (shafa'ah) of the prophets, then the scholars, then the martyrs, then the rest of the believers, each according to his status and station. And whoever among the believers remains and has no intercessor is brought out by the grace of Allah Almighty, and no believer will abide eternally in the Fire; rather, whoever has the weight of an atom of faith in his heart will come out of it. And he believes in the superiority of the Companions and their ranking: that the best of people after the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) is Abu Bakr, then Umar, then Uthman, then Ali (may Allah be pleased with them all). And he thinks well of all the Companions and praises them as Allah and His Messenger have praised them. All of this is because of the reports (akhbar) that have come and the traditions (athar) that have witnessed. So whoever believes all of this with certainty is among the people of truth and the group of the Sunnah, and has left the band of misguidance and innovation. So we ask Allah Almighty for complete certainty and steadfastness in religion for us and for all Muslims. Indeed, He is the Most Merciful of the merciful. And may Allah bless Muhammad and all his family.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage is a creedal conclusion that covers the reckoning (hisab), intercession (shafa'ah), the eventual removal of monotheists from Hell, the ranking of the Companions, and the necessity of good opinion of them. It begins by describing the variations among people on the Day of Reckoning: some are scrutinized strictly, some are shown leniency, and some enter Paradise without any reckoning – these are the 'muqarrabun' (the close ones). Allah asks the prophets about delivering the message, the disbelievers about denying the messengers, the innovators about following the Sunnah, and the Muslims about their deeds. Then the passage affirms that monotheists (muwahhidun) will be removed from Hell after punishment, by Allah's grace, so that no monotheist remains in Hell. Intercession is described in a hierarchy: prophets, then scholars, then martyrs, then the rest of the believers, each according to his station. Those without an intercessor are brought out by Allah's grace; no believer remains in Hell forever – anyone with even an atom's weight of faith in his heart will eventually exit. Then the belief in the superiority of the Companions is stated: the best after the Prophet is Abu Bakr, then Umar, then Uthman, then Ali. One must think well of all Companions and praise them as Allah and His Messenger have. All these beliefs are based on reported narrations (akhbar) and transmitted traditions (athar). The passage concludes that whoever holds these beliefs with certainty is from the people of truth and the group of the Sunnah, and has separated from the people of misguidance and innovation. It ends with a prayer for steadfastness.

A) Prophets

?

?

Intercession and the Removal of Monotheists from Hell
Ibn Asakir affirms intercession by prophets, scholars, martyrs, and believers, and the eventual removal of all monotheists from Hell.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni belief in intercession (shafa'ah) and that all monotheists will eventually be removed from Hell by Allah's grace, even if they have only an atom's weight of faith.

Core Idea
No believer remains in Hell forever; intercession and divine grace ensure their eventual salvation.

One of the distinguishing beliefs of Ahl al-Sunnah is that monotheists will not abide eternally in Hell. This lesson covers the hierarchy of intercession and the ultimate removal of all believers from the Fire, emphasizing Allah's mercy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on intercession and removal
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the statement about removal of monotheists and the hierarchy of intercession.
2
Identify the hierarchy of intercessors
Find the order: prophets, then scholars, then martyrs, then other believers. Each intercedes according to their station.
3
Understand the fate of those without an intercessor
The passage says they are brought out by Allah's grace. No believer remains in Hell eternally.
Even the weight of an atom of faith guarantees eventual exit.
4
Reflect on the theological implications
This belief contrasts with groups that hold that sinful believers may be eternally punished. It emphasizes Allah's mercy.

And may Allah bless Muhammad and all his family.

?

?

The Rank and Status of the Companions
Ibn Asakir states the doctrinal ranking of the Companions and the obligation to have a good opinion of them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position on the ranking of the Companions (Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, Ali) and the obligation to think well of all of them.

Core Idea
The Companions are ranked in virtue, and we must hold a good opinion of all of them as praised by Allah and His Messenger.

This final part of the creed establishes the belief in the superiority of the first four caliphs in order and the imperative to love and praise all Companions. It also ties these beliefs to being part of the people of the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the Companions
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the specific ranking of the four caliphs and the command to think well of all Companions.
2
Understand the ranking
The best after the Prophet is Abu Bakr, then Umar, then Uthman, then Ali. This is a doctrinal belief.
3
Recognize the obligation to praise all Companions
We must think well of all Companions and praise them as Allah and His Messenger did.
4
See the conclusion
Holding these beliefs with certainty distinguishes the people of truth from innovation. The passage ends with a prayer.

Variation in Reckoning and Questioning
Ibn 'Asakir enumerates the varying judgment categories and questioning of groups.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three categories of people regarding reckoning on the Day of Judgment and the specific questions each group will face.

Core Idea
How you are judged depends on who you are and what you were responsible for.

Ibn 'Asakir begins by describing the varying states of people in the Hereafter: some are scrutinized, some treated leniently, and some enter Paradise without any reckoning. He then explains that different groups will be asked about different things according to their roles. This passage lays out the divine justice and mercy in the questioning process.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Then read the translation to understand the three categories of reckoning and the four groups questioned.
Notice that the muqarrabūn enter Paradise without any reckoning.
2
Identify the three categories of reckoning
The passage names three types: those scrutinized, those given leniency, and those who enter without reckoning. Think about what each implies about a person's state.
3
Identify the four groups questioned
List the four groups: prophets, disbelievers, innovators, and Muslims. Note what each is asked about. This shows accountability is tailored.
Ask yourself why innovators are asked about the Sunnah specifically.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتفاوت الخلق فيه إلى مناقش فى الحساب وإلى مسامح فيه ، إلى من يدخل الجنة بغير حساب وهم المقربون فيسأل من شاء من الأنبياء عن تبليغ الرسالة ومن شاء من الكفار عن تكذيب المرسلين ويسأل المبتدعة عن السنة ويسأل المسلمين عن الأعمال ويؤمن بإخراج الموحدين من النار بعد الانتقام حتى لا يبقى في جهنم موحد بفضل الله تعالى ، ويؤمن بشفاعة الأنبياء ثم العلماء ثم الشهداء ثم سائر المؤمنين كل على حسب جاهه ومنزلته ، ومن بقى من المؤمنين ولم يكن له شفيع أخرج بفضل الله تعالى ولا يخلد في النار مؤمن بل يخرج منها من كان في قلبه مثقال ذرة من الإيمان ، وأن يعتقد فضل الصحابة وترتيبهم وأن أفضل الناس بعد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أبو بكر ثم عمر ثم عثمان ثم على رضى الله عنهم ، وأن يحسن الظن بجميع الصحابة ويثني عليهم كما أثنى الله تعالى ورسوله عليه السلام وعليهم أجمعين فكل ذلك لما وردت به الاخبار وشهدت به الآثار فمن اعتقد جميع ذلك موقنا به كان من أهل الحق وعصابة السنة وفارق رهط الضلال والبدعة فنسأل الله تعالى كمال اليقين والثبات في الدين لنا ولكافة المسلمين إنه أرحم الراحمين وصلى الله على محمد وآله أجمعين
And the people vary in it: one who is scrutinized in reckoning, and one who is given leniency in it, and one who enters Paradise without reckoning – they are the ones brought near (al-muqarrabūn). So He asks whom He wills of the prophets about conveying the message, and whom He wills of the disbelievers about denying the messengers, and He asks the innovators (al-mubtadi‘a) about the Sunnah, and He asks the Muslims about deeds. And he believes in the removal of the monotheists (al-muwaḥḥidūn) from the Fire after punishment, until no monotheist remains in Hell by the grace of God (faḍl Allāh). And he believes in the intercession (shafā‘a) of the prophets, then the scholars, then the martyrs, then the rest of the believers, each according to his rank and station. And whoever remains among the believers and has no intercessor is brought out by the grace of God, and no believer will abide eternally in the Fire; rather, whoever has in his heart a mustard seed’s weight of faith will be brought out of it. And that one should believe in the merit (faḍl) of the Companions (ṣaḥāba) and their ranking, and that the best of people after the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) are Abū Bakr, then ‘Umar, then ‘Uthmān, then ‘Alī (may God be pleased with them). And that one should think well of all the Companions and praise them as God and His Messenger (peace be upon him) praised them, all of them. For all that is due to what the reports have conveyed and the traditions have testified. So whoever believes all of that, convinced of it, is among the people of truth and the party of the Sunnah, and has separated from the band of misguidance and innovation (al-bid‘a). So we ask God Almighty for complete certainty and steadfastness in the religion for us and for all Muslims; He is the Most Merciful of the merciful. And may God bless Muḥammad and his family, all of them.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage is a creedal summary covering eschatological beliefs and the virtues of the Companions. It first describes the varying states of people on the Day of Judgment regarding reckoning: some are scrutinized, some are given leniency, and some enter Paradise without any reckoning – these are the muqarrabūn. Then it mentions that God will question different groups: prophets about conveying the message, disbelievers about denying the messengers, innovators (mubtadi‘a) about the Sunnah, and ordinary Muslims about their deeds. The passage then affirms the belief (using 'he believes' as a statement of creed) that monotheists will be removed from the Fire after they have been punished, by God's grace, until no monotheist remains in Hell. It also affirms intercession (shafā‘a) by prophets, scholars, martyrs, and other believers, each according to their rank, and that even those without an intercessor will be brought out by God's grace. The text explicitly states that no believer will remain eternally in the Fire; anyone with even a mustard seed's weight of faith will eventually be brought out. Next, the passage turns to the Companions: one must believe in their merit and ranking, affirming that the best after the Prophet are Abu Bakr, then Umar, then Uthman, then Ali. One must think well of all the Companions and praise them as God and His Messenger praised them. The passage concludes by stating that whoever believes all of this is from the people of truth (ahl al-ḥaqq) and the party of the Sunnah, and has separated from misguidance and innovation. It ends with a prayer for certainty and steadfastness.

Key Terms
المقربون (al-muqarrabūn)
المبتدعة (al-mubtadi‘a)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that only disbelievers are questioned or that all people are questioned about the same thing.
Correction: The passage shows that different groups are asked about different matters according to their roles, and believers who enter without reckoning are not questioned.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who enters Paradise without any reckoning?
A) The prophets
B) The disbelievers
C) The muqarrabūn
D) The innovators

Key Takeaway
Divine judgment is tailored: the muqarrabūn enter without reckoning, and each group is asked about its specific responsibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You know that the muqarrabun enter Paradise without reckoning. Is your heart set on being among them, or are you content with being merely scrutinized? What one step will you take today to draw closer to Allah so that you might hope to be of those brought near?
?
This passage mentions that innovators will be asked about the Sunnah. Have you ever defended or practiced an innovation thinking it is good? What in your practice of Islam needs to be checked against the pure Sunnah?
?
Prophets will be asked about conveying their message. You are not a prophet, but you have a duty to convey the truth to those around you. Are you actively doing that? Write down one person you will speak to about Islam this week.

Removal from Hell and Intercession
Ibn 'Asakir affirms the removal of monotheists from Hell and the intercession chain.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the belief that all monotheists will eventually be removed from Hell, either through intercession or by God's grace, and that even a mustard seed of faith suffices for salvation.

Core Idea
No believer stays in Hell forever; God's mercy prevails over His punishment.

Having described the questioning, Ibn 'Asakir now affirms a core Sunni creed: all monotheists will eventually be taken out of Hell. He details the intercession of prophets, scholars, martyrs, and other believers, and then declares that anyone with even a mustard seed's weight of faith will be saved by God's grace. This passage emphasizes the ultimate triumph of divine mercy for believers.

Guided Path
1
Read about the removal of monotheists
Read the passage on the removal of monotheists from Hell after punishment, noting that it happens by God's grace.
The phrase 'until no monotheist remains in Hell' shows completeness of mercy.
2
Identify the hierarchy of intercessors
List the four groups: prophets, scholars, martyrs, and other believers. Note that intercession is according to rank.
Scholars come before martyrs in this hierarchy.
3
Understand the final guarantee
Read the last part: even those without an intercessor are brought out by God's grace, as long as they have faith.
The mustard seed analogy emphasizes minimal faith is sufficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتفاوت الخلق فيه إلى مناقش فى الحساب وإلى مسامح فيه ، إلى من يدخل الجنة بغير حساب وهم المقربون فيسأل من شاء من الأنبياء عن تبليغ الرسالة ومن شاء من الكفار عن تكذيب المرسلين ويسأل المبتدعة عن السنة ويسأل المسلمين عن الأعمال ويؤمن بإخراج الموحدين من النار بعد الانتقام حتى لا يبقى في جهنم موحد بفضل الله تعالى ، ويؤمن بشفاعة الأنبياء ثم العلماء ثم الشهداء ثم سائر المؤمنين كل على حسب جاهه ومنزلته ، ومن بقى من المؤمنين ولم يكن له شفيع أخرج بفضل الله تعالى ولا يخلد في النار مؤمن بل يخرج منها من كان في قلبه مثقال ذرة من الإيمان ، وأن يعتقد فضل الصحابة وترتيبهم وأن أفضل الناس بعد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أبو بكر ثم عمر ثم عثمان ثم على رضى الله عنهم ، وأن يحسن الظن بجميع الصحابة ويثني عليهم كما أثنى الله تعالى ورسوله عليه السلام وعليهم أجمعين فكل ذلك لما وردت به الاخبار وشهدت به الآثار فمن اعتقد جميع ذلك موقنا به كان من أهل الحق وعصابة السنة وفارق رهط الضلال والبدعة فنسأل الله تعالى كمال اليقين والثبات في الدين لنا ولكافة المسلمين إنه أرحم الراحمين وصلى الله على محمد وآله أجمعين
And the people vary in it: one who is scrutinized in reckoning, and one who is given leniency in it, and one who enters Paradise without reckoning – they are the ones brought near (al-muqarrabūn). So He asks whom He wills of the prophets about conveying the message, and whom He wills of the disbelievers about denying the messengers, and He asks the innovators (al-mubtadi‘a) about the Sunnah, and He asks the Muslims about deeds. And he believes in the removal of the monotheists (al-muwaḥḥidūn) from the Fire after punishment, until no monotheist remains in Hell by the grace of God (faḍl Allāh). And he believes in the intercession (shafā‘a) of the prophets, then the scholars, then the martyrs, then the rest of the believers, each according to his rank and station. And whoever remains among the believers and has no intercessor is brought out by the grace of God, and no believer will abide eternally in the Fire; rather, whoever has in his heart a mustard seed’s weight of faith will be brought out of it. And that one should believe in the merit (faḍl) of the Companions (ṣaḥāba) and their ranking, and that the best of people after the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) are Abū Bakr, then ‘Umar, then ‘Uthmān, then ‘Alī (may God be pleased with them). And that one should think well of all the Companions and praise them as God and His Messenger (peace be upon him) praised them, all of them. For all that is due to what the reports have conveyed and the traditions have testified. So whoever believes all of that, convinced of it, is among the people of truth and the party of the Sunnah, and has separated from the band of misguidance and innovation (al-bid‘a). So we ask God Almighty for complete certainty and steadfastness in the religion for us and for all Muslims; He is the Most Merciful of the merciful. And may God bless Muḥammad and his family, all of them.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage is a creedal summary covering eschatological beliefs and the virtues of the Companions. It first describes the varying states of people on the Day of Judgment regarding reckoning: some are scrutinized, some are given leniency, and some enter Paradise without any reckoning – these are the muqarrabūn. Then it mentions that God will question different groups: prophets about conveying the message, disbelievers about denying the messengers, innovators (mubtadi‘a) about the Sunnah, and ordinary Muslims about their deeds. The passage then affirms the belief (using 'he believes' as a statement of creed) that monotheists will be removed from the Fire after they have been punished, by God's grace, until no monotheist remains in Hell. It also affirms intercession (shafā‘a) by prophets, scholars, martyrs, and other believers, each according to their rank, and that even those without an intercessor will be brought out by God's grace. The text explicitly states that no believer will remain eternally in the Fire; anyone with even a mustard seed's weight of faith will eventually be brought out. Next, the passage turns to the Companions: one must believe in their merit and ranking, affirming that the best after the Prophet are Abu Bakr, then Umar, then Uthman, then Ali. One must think well of all the Companions and praise them as God and His Messenger praised them. The passage concludes by stating that whoever believes all of this is from the people of truth (ahl al-ḥaqq) and the party of the Sunnah, and has separated from misguidance and innovation. It ends with a prayer for certainty and steadfastness.

Key Terms
الموحدون (al-muwaḥḥidūn)
الشفاعة (shafā‘a)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that intercession is only for prophets, or that believers can remain in Hell forever if they committed major sins.
Correction: The passage affirms multiple ranks of intercessors and states that no believer will remain in Hell forever.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who intercedes after the prophets?
A) Martyrs
B) Scholars
C) The rest of the believers
D) Angels

Key Takeaway
Every believer, even a sinful one, will eventually leave Hell, either through intercession or directly by God's grace due to their faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that the mustard seed of faith in your heart guarantees your eventual salvation, or do you live in fear that your sins outweigh God's mercy? How would your daily actions change if you internalized this promise completely?
?
When you sin, do you remember that God has appointed intercessors—prophets, scholars, and martyrs—to plead for believers? How can you actively seek their intercession while still striving to obey?
?
If you were in Hell being punished for your sins, would you still have even a mustard seed's worth of faith? Reflect on whether your connection to Islam is deep enough that it would survive the fire—even momentarily—and what that says about your faith today.

Merit and Ranking of the Companions
Ibn 'Asakir states the ranking of the four caliphs and the duty to respect all Companions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni belief in the ranking of the four Rightly Guided Caliphs and the obligation to think well of all Companions.

Core Idea
The best of people after the Prophet are Abu Bakr, then 'Umar, then 'Uthman, then 'Ali, and all Companions deserve our good opinion.

Ibn 'Asakir now turns to a central tenet of Sunni orthodoxy: the virtues of the Companions. He establishes the well-known ranking of the four caliphs and stresses that we must think well of all Companions and praise them as God and His Messenger did. This passage distinguishes Sunni creed from groups that criticize the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Read the ranking of the caliphs
Read the passage on the Companions, paying attention to the specific order: Abu Bakr, then Umar, then Uthman, then Ali.
This order is a matter of creed, not just preference.
2
Note the command to think well of all Companions
The passage says to think well of all Companions and praise them as God and the Prophet praised them.
This excludes any criticism of any Companion.
3
Understand the consequence
Believing this makes one part of the people of truth and the Sunnah, separating from innovation.
The passage concludes with a prayer for steadfastness.

Divine Preservation Through Righteousness
Ibn Asakir combines Quranic exegesis and hadith to illustrate divine preservation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah preserves a believer's descendants and dwellings because of his righteousness, as shown in the Quran and hadith.

Core Idea
A believer's righteousness protects his children, grandchildren, and neighbors.

This lesson explores a profound blessing: Allah extends His protection to a believer's offspring and even neighboring homes due to the believer's piety. We begin with the Quranic story of al-Khidr and the two boys, then examine prophetic hadith that confirm this principle.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the English translation. Notice how the author connects the Quranic verse to the hadith.
The passage is a combination of commentary and prophetic traditions.
2
Identify the Quranic reference
Find the reference to Surah al-Kahf (18:82) about the two boys and the righteous father. Understand that Allah protected them because of their father's righteousness.
The righteous ancestor is said to be the seventh or ninth grandfather.
3
Examine the hadith
Read the hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri. Note that Allah preserves the believer in his child, grandchild, neighbor, and nine dwellings around him.
This shows the blessing extends beyond immediate family to the community.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider that righteousness is not automatically inherited; rather, it is a divine blessing granted due to the ancestor's piety. This encourages striving for personal righteousness.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

For indeed Allah the Mighty and Majestic only protected them and cared for them because He described their father as righteous, and preserved them until they reached their full strength so that they could extract their treasure by the blessing of their grandfather. It has come from some of the commentators commonly that that grandfather was the ninth or seventh. The shaykh al-imam Abu Nasr Abd al-Rahim ibn al-Ustadh Abi al-Qasim al-Qushayri (may Allah have mercy on them) wrote to me saying: I heard my father say: It was said concerning His statement (and their father was righteous) that this referred to the ninth or seventh grandfather, and that Allah buried that treasure, so al-Khidr was appointed to serve them out of honor for that. And it has come in the hadith: 'Verily Allah preserves the believer in his child and his child's child and his child's child's child.' Abu Ghalib Ahmad ibn al-Hasan ibn al-Banna narrated to us, saying: Abu al-Husayn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Abnusi al-Sayrafi narrated to us, saying: Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Umar ibn Ahmad ibn Mahdi al-Daraqutni narrated to us, saying: Abu al-Abbas Abd Allah ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim al-Maristani narrated to us, saying: al-Qasim ibn Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab narrated to us, saying: Abd al-Aziz ibn al-Nu'man al-Mawsili Abu al-Hasan narrated to us, saying: Amr ibn Atiyya narrated to us from Atiyya from Abi Sa'id who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Verily Allah preserves the believer in his child and his child's child and his neighbor and his neighbor's neighbor and nine dwellings around him.' Al-Daraqutni said: 'Umara al-Kufi alone narrated it from Amr ibn Atiyya from his father. I said: Al-Hasan ibn [?] also narrated it from Atiyya. Al-Shaykh Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Ahmad informed us, saying: Abu al-Qasim Abd Allah ibn Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn al-Khallal informed us, saying: Abu al-Hasan Muhammad ibn Uthman ibn Muhammad ibn Uthman ibn Shihab al-Daqqaq al-Nafari narrated to us, saying: al-Husayn ibn Isma'il al-Mahamili narrated to us, saying: Ya'qub ibn Ibrahim al-Dawraqi narrated to us, saying: Shu'ayb ibn Harb narrated to us, saying: al-Hasan ibn 'Umara narrated to us, saying: Atiyya al-'Awfi narrated to us from Abi Sa'id al-Khudri who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Verily Allah preserves the believer in his child and his child's child and his child's child's child and He preserves the believer in his dwelling and his neighbor's dwelling and his neighbor's neighbor's dwelling.' And al-Shaykh Abu al-Qasim Hibat Allah ibn Muhammad al-Shaybani informed us, saying: al-Qadi Abu al-Qasim Ali ibn al-Muhsin al-Tanukhi narrated to us, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Abd Allah ibn Julayz al-Dawraqi narrated to us, saying: Hamza ibn al-Muttalib al-Khuza'i narrated to us, saying: Abu al-Abbas Isma'il ibn al-Haytham al-Abdi narrated to us, saying: Mubarak Abu Sahim narrated to us from Abd al-Aziz from Suhayb from Anas who said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Verily Allah preserves the righteous servant among his family and children and the dwellings around him.' Abu Bakr al-Khatib al-Hafiz al-Tanukhi narrated it. And the two shaykhs Abu al-Qasim ibn al-Samarqandi and Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Hibat Allah ibn Abd al-Salam al-Katib informed us, both saying: Abd Allah ibn Muhammad al-Khatib narrated to us, saying: Ubayd Allah ibn Muhammad ibn Hubaba narrated to us, saying: Abd Allah ibn Muhammad al-Baghawi narrated to us, saying: Ibn al-Muqri'—meaning Muhammad ibn Abd Allah ibn Yazid—narrated to us, saying: Sufyan narrated to us from Ibn Suqah from al-Munkadir who said: Allah the Mighty and Majestic sets right by the righteousness of a man his child and his child's child and the people of his dwelling and the dwellings around them, and they continue in the protection and preservation of Allah. Abu al-Qasim Zahir ibn Tahir informed us, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn informed us, saying: Abu Abd Allah al-Hafiz informed us, saying: Abu al-Abbas—he is al-Asamm—narrated to us, saying: Muhammad ibn al-Nu'man in Bayt al-Maqdis narrated to us, saying: Nu'aym ibn Hammad narrated to us, saying: Ibn al-Mubarak narrated to us from Muhammad ibn Suqah from Ibn al-Munkadir who said: Verily Allah the Mighty and Majestic sets right by the righteousness of his father his child and his child's child and preserves him in his dwelling and the dwellings around him as long as they are in them.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage is a collection of hadith and early sayings establishing the principle that Allah preserves the believer's offspring and dwellings due to the righteousness of an ancestor. The author begins by referencing the Quranic story of al-Khidr and the two boys (al-Kahf: 82), where Allah protected them because their father was righteous. He notes that some exegetes said that righteous ancestor was the seventh or ninth grandfather. Then he cites a saying from Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri linking the verse to the concept of preservation. The author then provides multiple hadith chains from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri and Anas ibn Malik, in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) states that Allah preserves the believer in his children, grandchildren, and even neighboring dwellings. One version adds 'nine dwellings around him' and another mentions 'his dwelling and his neighbor's dwelling and his neighbor's neighbor's dwelling.' After each chain, the author occasionally adds critical remarks, such as noting that one narrator was unique in transmitting it. He also includes statements from early authorities like Ibn al-Munkadir, who affirm that Allah sets right a man's descendants and dwellings because of his righteousness. The overall argument is that a righteous person's blessing extends to his progeny and community, preserving them through Allah's protection.

Key Terms
صلاح
حفظ
بركة
دويرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That righteousness is automatically inherited by descendants, so children are always righteous if parents are.
Correction: The hadith shows Allah preserves descendants as a blessing due to the ancestor's piety, not that they inherit the trait. It is a divine favor, not an automatic inheritance.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited by Ibn Asakir, what does Allah preserve for the believer?
A) Only the believer himself
B) The believer's wealth and property
C) The believer's children and dwellings around him
D) Only the believer's immediate family

Key Takeaway
Allah preserves a believer's descendants and nearby dwellings as a blessing flowing from the believer's righteousness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you aware that your righteousness or lack thereof may affect your children, grandchildren, and even your neighbors right now? What one change in your practice of faith today could leave a protective blessing for them?
?
The hadith mentions 'nine dwellings around him'. Who in your immediate community could benefit from your piety? Which neighbor have you neglected in your supplications or acts of kindness?
?
If you have (or plan to have) children, what spiritual inheritance are you building for them? Will your actions today cause Allah to preserve them after you're gone, or will your negligence leave them exposed?

The Prophet's Mercy: Refusing to Curse the Polytheists
Ibn Asakir narrates the hadith of the Prophet's refusal to curse the polytheists.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Prophet's mission was one of mercy, not cursing, as demonstrated by his refusal to curse even the polytheists.

Core Idea
The Prophet was sent as mercy, not a curser.

In this passage, Ibn Asakir presents a powerful hadith that illustrates the Prophet's character. When asked to curse the polytheists, the Prophet declined, stating that he was sent only as a mercy. This sets the standard for how believers should treat even those who oppose them.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith with its chain
Read the Arabic passage slowly, noting the names of narrators. Understand that the chain lends authenticity.
The chain is long but shows careful transmission.
2
Identify the Prophet's response
Find the Prophet's words: 'I was not sent as a curser; I was only sent as a mercy.' Reflect on the contrast.
3
Consider the implication
Think about why the Prophet refused to curse polytheists. What does this teach about his character and mission?
This is a lesson in mercy even towards enemies.

Source Text

And the Messenger of the Lord of the Worlds, may God bless him and his family and all his companions, refrained from cursing those who were asked about cursing from the polytheists, despite their adherence to polytheism. This is narrated from Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn al-Fadl al-Farawi and Abu al-Muzaffar Abd al-Mun'im ibn Abd al-Karim al-Qushayri, both said: Abu Sa'd Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn Muhammad al-Jinzirudhi told us, he said: Abu Amr Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn al-Hayri told us... (chain continues)... Abu Huraira said: It was said (and in the hadith of Ibn Hamdan: I said), O Messenger of God, pray against the polytheists! He said: 'I was not sent as a curser; I was only sent as a mercy.' Muslim narrated it in his Sahih from Muhammad ibn Abbad. So if the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, did not see cursing the polytheists, how then did al-Ahwazi permit in his religion the cursing of devout scholars? Thus he was not guided by God's guidance, nor did he follow his Prophet, but rather he was blind to the path of guidance and threw himself into what leads to destruction. Did he think he would be left unchecked when he erred in what he said about al-Ash'ari and transgressed, and followed the desire of the accursed Satan in cursing the Muslims, while he avoided refraining from them and overlooking? God Almighty said in His noble Book: 'Satan only desires to cause enmity and hatred among you.' So who is more astray than one who follows his desire and exhausts his strength in falsely blaming scholars, and observes neither covenant nor protection towards them, nor regards any station or sanctity? And who is more ignorant than one who devotes himself to slandering and attacking the great and notable scholars of the Sharia? Had he considered what he said thoughtfully, he would know that he committed a reprehensible matter. Had he been knowledgeable in the rulings of Sharia, he would be certain that he committed a great sin. It suffices as an abandonment of truth and avoidance of it that he considered the falsehood he mentioned against him as a pious deed. How fortunate would he have been if he escaped from what he mentioned unscathed and came out clean without harm. But how can he have safety when he has left the path of uprightness? And if he had said instead...
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage provides a prophetic proof against al-Ahwazi's cursing. Ibn Asakir narrates a hadith with a full chain: the Prophet was asked to curse the polytheists, but he replied, 'I was not sent as a curser; I was only sent as a mercy.' The author then applies this: if the Prophet refrained from cursing polytheists despite their greater sin, then al-Ahwazi's cursing of devout scholars is even more reprehensible. He condemns al-Ahwazi for following Satan, who incites enmity and hatred, as per Quran 5:91. He then declares that al-Ahwazi is astray and ignorant, having abandoned truth and considered his false accusations as piety. The author ends with a rhetorical wish that al-Ahwazi had escaped unscathed, but notes that he has left the path of uprightness. The passage is incomplete at the end of the page.

Key Terms
اللعن
المشركين
الرحمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Cursing polytheists is always permissible and encouraged.
Correction: The Prophet refused to curse polytheists, showing that mercy is preferred over cursing even for the worst sinners.

Checkpoint
What did the Prophet say when asked to curse the polytheists?
A) He cursed them.
B) He said he was sent as a mercy.
C) He remained silent.
D) He prayed for their guidance.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's refusal to curse polytheists demonstrates that his mission was fundamentally one of mercy, not condemnation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When someone wrongs you deeply, do you instinctively wish for their destruction or do you hope for their guidance? How can you emulate the Prophet's mercy in your personal conflicts today?
?
Think about your own words: How often do you curse or wish ill upon others, even in your heart? What does that say about your connection to the Prophet's way?
?
The polytheists were the worst enemies of Islam, yet the Prophet showed mercy. Who in your life do you consider 'unforgivable'? Are you willing to let go of your desire for retribution and pray for their guidance instead?

Cursing Scholars: An Analogy with the Prophet's Example
Ibn Asakir applies the prophetic example to condemn the cursing of scholars by al-Ahwazi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Asakir uses the Prophet's example to condemn the cursing of scholars, and why such cursing is a grave sin.

Core Idea
If the Prophet did not curse polytheists, cursing scholars is far worse.

Building on the hadith, Ibn Asakir turns the argument against al-Ahwazi. He reasons that if the Prophet refrained from cursing polytheists despite their major sin, then cursing devout scholars—who are far more virtuous—is an even greater transgression. This lesson explores that analogy and its consequences.

Guided Path
1
Understand the analogy
Ibn Asakir argues from the greater to the lesser: if the Prophet did not curse polytheists, then al-Ahwazi's cursing of scholars is even more reprehensible.
Scholars are of higher status than polytheists.
2
Examine the Quranic quote
The verse from Surah al-Ma'idah (5:91) is cited to show that cursing fosters enmity and hatred, which is Satan's desire.
3
Appreciate the condemnation's severity
Ibn Asakir uses strong rhetorical questions to highlight the ignorance and astrayness of al-Ahwazi. Note the language of 'falsehood' and 'great sin'.
This shows the gravity of attacking scholars.

The Prohibition of Cursing and the True Believer
Ibn Asakir presents hadith proofs that the believer does not curse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that cursing is incompatible with complete faith, based on prophetic hadiths and the commentary of Ibn Asakir.

Core Idea
The believer does not curse; cursing contradicts perfect faith.

In this passage, Ibn Asakir presents two clear hadiths that establish a fundamental moral trait of the believer: he is not a curser. The first is a personal advice from the Prophet to an individual, the second a general statement about believers. The author then explains that perfect faith restrains one from cursing, while weakness in faith leads to slander and accusation.

Guided Path
1
Read the first hadith
Notice the chain of narration and the advice given to Jarmuz al-Hujaymi: 'I advise you not to be a curser.' Reflect on how this is a direct command.
The word 'la'aan' means one who curses frequently.
2
Read the second hadith
Ibn 'Umar reports the Prophet's words: 'The believer is not a curser.' Understand this as a description of the believer's nature.
This hadith is also recorded by al-Tirmidhi.
3
Consider the author's conclusion
Ibn Asakir explains that the perfect believer does not hasten to curse, while the forsaken one follows Satan by slandering others. Connect this to your own understanding of faith.
Cursing is seen as a sign of weak certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أبو بكر أحمد بن جعفر بن حمدان قال ثنا عبد الله بن أحمد بن محمد بن حنبل ، قال حدثني أبي قال ثنا عبد الصمد يعني ابن عبد الوارث قال ثنا الله عبيد بن هوذة القريعي أنه قال حدثنى رجل سمع جرموز الهجيمي قال قلت يا رسول الله أوصنى قال ) أوصيك أن لا تكون لعانا ( . وأخبرنا الشيخ أبو عبد الله الخلال الاصبهاني قال أنا أبو القسم إبراهيم بن منصور الخباز قال أنا أبو بكر بن المقرى قال أنا أبو يعلى أحمد ابن على الموصلى قال ثنا محمد بن بشار بندار قال ثنا أبو عامر قال ثنا كثير بن زيد المدني قال سمعت سالم بن عبد الله يحدث عن أبيه قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ) لا يكون المؤمن لعانا ( رواه الترمذي في جامعه عن بندار . والأحاديث في هذا المعنى كثيرة متسعة وهذه التي أوردتها في المعنى ههنا مقنعة ، فالمؤمن الكامل الإيمان هو الذي لا يتسارع إلى اللعن والمخذول الضعيف الايقان يمتثل أمر الشيطان له بالوقيعة في الناس والطعن :
Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ja'far ibn Hamdan said: 'Abdullah ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Hanbal narrated to us: my father narrated to me: 'Abd al-Samad, meaning ibn 'Abd al-Warith, narrated to us: 'Allah Ubayd ibn Hawdha al-Qurashi narrated to us that he said: a man who heard Jarmuz al-Hujaymi narrated to me: I said: O Messenger of Allah, advise me. He said: I advise you not to be a curser.) And the shaykh Abu 'Abdullah al-Khallal al-Isfahani informed us: Abu al-Qasim Ibrahim ibn Mansur al-Khabbaz informed us: Abu Bakr ibn al-Muqri' informed us: Abu Ya'la Ahmad ibn 'Ali al-Mawsili informed us: Muhammad ibn Bashshar Bundar narrated to us: Abu 'Amir narrated to us: Kathir ibn Zayd al-Madani narrated to us: I heard Salim ibn 'Abdullah narrating from his father: the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: The believer is not a curser.) al-Tirmidhi narrated it in his Jami' from Bundar. And the hadiths in this meaning are many and extensive, and these that I have mentioned here in this meaning are convincing. So the believer complete in faith is the one who does not hasten to curse, while the forsaken one weak in certainty obeys the command of Satan against himself by slandering people and accusing them.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage presents two hadith proofs forbidding cursing, followed by the author's commentary. The first hadith is from Jarmuz al-Hujaymi who asked the Prophet for advice and was told not to be a curser (la'aan). The second hadith from Ibn 'Umar states that the believer (mu'min) is not a curser. The author notes that many hadiths convey this meaning, and these are sufficient. He then explains that the perfect believer is the one who does not rush to curse, whereas the forsaken person with weak certainty follows Satan's command to slander and accuse people. The passage emphasizes that cursing is incompatible with complete faith.

Key Terms
لعن
مؤمن
لعان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A believer may curse occasionally without affecting his faith.
Correction: The Prophet said the believer is not a curser, and Ibn Asakir explains that the perfect believer does not hasten to curse. Cursing is incompatible with complete faith.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited from Ibn 'Umar, what is said about the believer?
A) The believer is often a curser.
B) The believer is not a curser.
C) The believer may curse in self-defense.
D) The believer must curse to defend Islam.

Key Takeaway
A true believer does not curse; avoiding cursing is a sign of complete faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When anger flares, do curses slip from your tongue before you can stop them? What specific habit or environment triggers this, and what will you do today to guard your tongue in those moments?
?
You have read that the believer is not a curser. Are there justifications you use—'I'm venting', 'They deserve it', 'It's just a joke'—that allow you to curse without repentance? Will you commit to a 30-day challenge to eliminate all forms of cursing from your speech and see how your faith feels?
?
The forsaken one is described as weak in certainty. What does your own certainty look like when you curse? Is it strong? If not, what is one verse or hadith you will memorize and repeat to strengthen your iman so that your tongue reflects true belief?

A Prophetic Sign: The Last Cursing the First
Ibn Asakir cites a hadith linking end-times curse to slander of Imams.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the prophetic sign that the later generations of the Ummah will curse the earlier righteous, and how this applies to the slander of Imam Ahmad by the Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
Cursing early righteous is a sign of the end, not a flaw in them.

Ibn Asakir presents a hadith from 'A'isha that warns of a time when the later generations will curse the earlier ones. He then connects this to the attacks of the Mu'tazila against Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal, showing that such slander is a fulfillment of the prophecy and not a reflection on the imam's standing.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its chain
Examine the chain of narration and the text of the hadith from 'A'isha. Notice that the Prophet explicitly states that the Ummah will not perish until the last generation curses the first.
The chain is long but indicates the hadith's transmission.
2
Understand the prophecy
The hadith warns that cursing the earlier righteous is a sign of the end times. It is not about the actual status of those cursed but about the moral decline of later generations.
3
See the application to Imam Ahmad
Ibn Asakir connects the hadith to his own time, pointing out that the Mu'tazila slandered Imam Ahmad. This shows that such attacks are predicted and do not diminish the imam's virtue.
The passage ends abruptly but the point is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد أخبرنا الشيخ أبو عبد الله الحسين بن عبد الملك الخلال قال أنا أبو القسم إبراهيم بن منصور السلمي قال أنا أبو بكر محمد بن إبراهيم بن المقرى قال أنا على بن منير بن دينار الواسطى قال ثنا أحمد بن زكريا قال ثنا عبد الله بن نمير عن إسماعيل بن إبراهيم بن مهاجر بن عمير من مسروق عن عائشة رضي الله عنها قالت أمروا بالاستغفار لهم قسبوهم ، أما أني سمعت نبيكم صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول ( لا تفنى هذه الأمة حتى يلعن آخرها أولها ( ولو وقفتم على ما يقول كل معتزلى مخبل فى حق الإمام أبي عبد الله بن أحمد بن محمد ابن حنبل مما قد نزهه الله عنه وبراً قدره ودينه منه ، ولذلك قيـل مـا أخـبـرنـا عن عبد الملك
And the shaykh Abu 'Abdullah al-Husayn ibn 'Abd al-Malik al-Khallal informed us: Abu al-Qasim Ibrahim ibn Mansur al-Sulami informed us: Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Ibrahim ibn al-Muqri' informed us: 'Ali ibn Munir ibn Dinar al-Wasiti informed us: Ahmad ibn Zakariyya narrated to us: 'Abdullah ibn Numayr narrated to us from Isma'il ibn Ibrahim ibn Muhajir ibn 'Umayr from Masruq from 'A'isha (may Allah be pleased with her) who said: They were commanded to seek forgiveness for them, but they cursed them. Indeed, I heard your Prophet (peace be upon him) say: 'This Ummah will not perish until its last generation curses its first generation.' And if you were to know what every deranged Mu'tazili says about the Imam Abu 'Abdullah, the imam, Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Hanbal (may Allah purify him from that [slander] and absolve his standing and religion from it), and for that reason it was said what we were informed from 'Abd al-Malik...
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage introduces a third tradition supporting the theme: a hadith from 'A'isha that the Ummah's last generation will curse its first. The chain is given, and the hadith text states that the Ummah will not perish until the last curses the first. Then the author ties this to his time: even the great Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal was slandered by the Mu'tazila. The passage is incomplete (cut off at 'Abd al-Malik), but the point is that such slander is a sign of the predicted curse and should not surprise the righteous. It reinforces the previous argument that criticism of al-Ash'ari is part of a broader pattern of cursing the pious.

Key Terms
يلعن آخرها أولها
معتزلى
أحمد بن حنبل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that being cursed or slandered proves that a person is misguided or blameworthy.
Correction: The hadith teaches that the later generation cursing the earlier is a sign of the end times and a condemnation of the cursers, not of those cursed. The slander of Imam Ahmad by the Mu'tazila is thus a fulfillment of prophecy and does not diminish his status.

Checkpoint
What did 'A'isha report that the Prophet said about the Ummah?
A) The best of them are the first generation.
B) The last generation will curse the first generation.
C) The Ummah will be divided into 73 sects.
D) The Ummah will never curse its scholars.

Key Takeaway
The hadith from 'A'isha warns that the last generation will curse the first, and Ibn Asakir uses this to show that slander of righteous imams like Ahmad is a predicted sign of the end, not a mark against them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever spoken ill of a righteous predecessor, even in jest? How does this hadith convict you of the gravity of such speech?
?
This lesson warns that cursing the early righteous is a sign of the end. Do you see any such attitudes in yourself or your community? What concrete step will you take to honor the salaf instead?
?
If the slander of Imam Ahmad is a fulfillment of prophecy, how should you respond when you hear similar slander against the Companions or early imams today? Is your silence complicity?

The Virtue of Defending a Muslim's Honor
Two hadiths on the reward for defending a Muslim's honor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the immense reward promised for defending a fellow Muslim's honor in his absence, as taught by multiple authentic hadiths.

Core Idea
Defending a brother's honor obligates Allah to protect you from Hellfire.

The Prophet ﷺ emphasized the duty of defending fellow Muslims' reputations. This lesson presents two hadiths transmitted through reliable chains, showing that such defense is a means of salvation from the Fire. The second hadith even includes a Quranic verse to reinforce the promise.

Guided Path
1
Read the two hadiths
Read the Arabic text of the two hadiths along with their translation. Notice the common theme of 'defending the flesh/honor' and the reward of being freed from Fire.
2
Identify the chains
Note the chains of transmission: the first from bint Yazid, the second from Abu Darda' via Shahr ibn Hawshab. Recognize the careful preservation of isnad.
This shows the importance of hadith verification.
3
Understand the reward
Both hadiths promise that Allah will protect the defender from Hellfire. Reflect on the magnitude of this reward.
4
Connect to the Quran
The second hadith includes recitation of Quran 30:47, connecting the promise to Allah's established practice of helping believers.
This reinforces the certainty of the reward.

Then Allah, the Generous, revived our hearts with the light of faith and wisdom, and forgave us our sins for love of our brothers who preceded us in faith, from the imams, and expiated our sins as He bestowed upon us the completion of favor and covered our faults by our defending the reputations of the predecessors of the Ummah, and granted us what He promised on the tongue of His Chosen Prophet, the Beloved, regarding one who defends the flesh of his Muslim brother in his absence. Among what the Shaykh Abu al-Qasim Hibatullah ibn Muhammad al-Shaybani informed us, he said: Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Ali al-Tamimi told us, he said: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ja'far al-Qati'i told us, he said: Abdullah ibn Ahmad ibn Hanbal told us, he said: My father narrated to me, he said: Muhammad Bakr told us, he said: Ubaydullah ibn Abi Ziyad told us, he said: Shahr ibn Hawshab narrated from bint Yazid, she said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: "Whoever defends the flesh of his brother in [his] absence, it is a right upon Allah Almighty to free him from the Fire." And the Shaykh Abu Ghalib Ahmad ibn al-Hasan ibn al-Banna informed us, he said: al-Hasan ibn Ali al-Jawhari told us, he said: Muhammad ibn al-Abbas ibn Hayawayh al-Khazzaz told us; and the two shaykhs Abu Ghalib also and his brother Abu Abdullah Yahya ibn al-Hasan informed us, they said: Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Abnusi told us, he said: Uthman ibn Amr ibn Muhammad ibn al-Mintab told us, they said: Yahya ibn Muhammad ibn Sa'id told us, he said: al-Husayn ibn al-Hasan al-Marwazi told us, he said: Amr ibn Uthman al-Kilabi informed us, he said: Musa ibn A'yan narrated from Layth from Shahr ibn Hawshab from Umm al-Darda' from Abu al-Darda', he said: I heard the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, say: "There is no Muslim who defends the honor of his brother except that it is a right upon Allah to repel the Fire of Hell from him on the Day of Resurrection, then he recited: 'And it is a right upon Us to help the believers.'" And the Shaykh Abu Sahl Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Isbahani informed us, he said: Abu al-Fadl Abd al-Rahman ibn Ahmad al-Razi told us, he said: Ja'far ibn Abdullah Fannaki told us, he said: Muhammad ibn Harun al-Ruyani told us, he said: Ibn Humayd told us, he said: Jarir narrated from Layth from Shahr from Umm al-Darda' from Abu al-Darda' from the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: "Whoever defends the honor of his brother in his absence, it is a right upon Allah to repel the Fire of Hell from him, then he recited: 'Indeed, We will support Our messengers and those who believe in the life of this world'—the verse." He said: And Muhammad ibn Harun narrated to us, he said: Amr ibn Ali told us, he said: Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rahman al-Tufawi Abu al-Mundhir told us, he said: Layth narrated from Shahr ibn Hawshab from Umm al-Darda' from Abu al-Darda', he said: I heard the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, say: "There is no man who defends the honor of his brother except that Allah defends him from the Fire of Hell on the Day of Resurrection, the day when witnesses stand, then he recited: 'Indeed, We will support Our messengers'—the verse." He said: And Muhammad ibn Harun al-Ruyani narrated to us, he said: Ahmad ibn Abd al-Rahman—meaning Ibn Wahb—told us, he said: ibn Yazid from [?] told us, he said: Muhammad ibn Muslim narrated from Sadaqah—meaning Abd Bassar—that Umm al-Darda' said: I heard Abu al-Darda' say: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: "Whoever defends the honor of his brother in his absence, Paradise becomes obligatory for him." And the Shaykh Abu Ghalib ibn al-Banna informed us, he said: Abu Muhammad al-Hasan ibn Ali told us, he said: Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Isma'il and Abu Umar al-Khazzaz told us, he said: Yahya ibn Muhammad ibn Sa'id told us, he said: al-Husayn ibn al-Hasan told us, he said: Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak informed us, he said: Ibn Ayyub narrated from Abdullah ibn Sulayman, that Isma'il ibn Yahya al-Ma'afiri informed him from Sahl ibn Mu'adh ibn Asad al-Juhani, from his father from the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: "Whoever protects a believer from a hypocrite in his absence, Allah will send an angel to him on the Day of Resurrection to protect him from the Fire of Hell; and whoever accuses a Muslim of something intending to disgrace him, Allah will detain him on the bridge of Hell until he comes out from what he said." Ahmad ibn Hanbal narrated it from Ahmad ibn al-Hajjaj and Ya'mur and Bishr al-Marwaziyyin, from Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak. And the Shaykh Abu Sahl Muhammad ibn Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Sa'duwayh al-Muzakki informed us in Baghdad, he said: Abu al-Fadl Abd al-Rahman ibn Ahmad ibn al-Hasan al-Razi al-Muqri' told us, he said: Abu al-Qasim Ja'far ibn Abdullah ibn Ya'qub ibn Fannaki told us, he said: Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Harun al-Ruyani told us, he said: Muhammad ibn Ishaq told us, he said: Ubaydullah ibn Musa told us, he said: Ibn Abi Layla narrated from al-Hakam from Bilal ibn Abi al-Darda' from his father, he said: A man spoke ill of another man in the presence of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and a man defended him, so the Messenger of Allah said: "Whoever defends the honor of his brother, it will be a shield from the Fire for him." Others narrated it from Ubaydullah and said: from Ibn Abi al-Darda' and did not name Bilal. And Sa'dan ibn Yahya al-Lakhmi narrated it from Ibn Abi Layla from al-Hakam from Abayah ibn Abi al-Darda', and he did not remember his name, and Abu al-Darda' does not have a son named Abayah. And Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Layla is weak in memory. And it was narrated from Ibn Abi Layla with another chain: Abu al-Barakat Abd al-Wahhab ibn al-Mubarak ibn Ahmad al-Hafiz informed us, he said: Abu al-Qasim Abd al-Aziz ibn Ali ibn Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Sukkari told us, he said: Abu Tahir Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Abbas al-Mukhlis told us, he said: Abu Muhammad Yahya ibn Muhammad ibn Sa'id told us by dictation in the year 313 in al-Muharram, he said: Abu Hisham Muhammad ibn Yazid al-Rifa'i told us, he said: Yahya ibn al-Yaman told us, he said: Ibn Abi Layla narrated from al-Hakam from Umm al-Darda' from Abu al-Darda', he said: A man spoke ill of another man in the presence of the Prophet, peace be upon him, and a man defended the honor of his brother, so he, peace be upon him, said: "Whoever defends the honor of his Muslim brother, it will be a shield from the Fire for him." The noble Abu al-Qasim Ali ibn Ibrahim informed us, he said: Abu al-Hasan Rasha ibn ...
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage is a collection of hadiths with multiple chains of transmission, all emphasizing the virtue and reward of defending a fellow Muslim's honor (عرض) in his absence. The author, Ibn Asakir, begins with a supplication and then presents several narrations. Each hadith states that whoever defends his brother's honor—whether by protecting his reputation, refuting slander, or shielding him from harm—Allah will protect him from the Fire of Hell on the Day of Resurrection, or make Paradise obligatory for him. Some versions include the recitation of Quranic verses (e.g., 'It is a right upon Us to help the believers,' 'Indeed, We will support Our messengers') to support the promise. The chains include well-known narrators such as Abu al-Darda', Umm al-Darda', Shahr ibn Hawshab, and others. The author also notes variations in chains and comments on the reliability of certain narrators (e.g., Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Layla is weak in memory, and an apparent confusion about the name of Abu al-Darda's son). The overall message is consistent: defending a Muslim's honor in his absence is a highly meritorious act that earns divine protection from Hellfire.

Key Terms
ذب عن لحم أخيه
عرض أخيه
المغيبة
يعتقه من النار
يرد عنه نار جهنم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Defending honor is limited to physical protection.
Correction: The hadiths explicitly mention 'defending the flesh' and 'honor' in absence, which includes verbal defense and refuting slander, not just physical actions.

Checkpoint
According to the hadiths in this passage, what is the reward for one who defends his brother's honor in his absence?
A) He will be given wealth in this world.
B) He will be protected from the Fire of Hell or enter Paradise.
C) He will be praised by people.
D) His sins will be forgiven without any condition.

Key Takeaway
Defending a Muslim's honor in his absence is a deed that earns Allah's guarantee of protection from Hellfire.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time you heard someone speaking ill of a fellow Muslim in their absence? Did you defend them or remain silent? How does this hadith make you feel about your inaction?
?
Are you quick to defend your own honor but hesitant to defend others? What does that reveal about your faith and brotherhood?
?
The Prophet ﷺ linked defending a brother's honor with Allah's promise of protection from Hellfire. If you knew that speaking up could save you from the Fire, would you have the courage to do so next time? What holds you back?
